2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Greenpeace,<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.greenpeace.org/new-zealand/campaign/the-green-covid-response-2020|title=The Green Covid Response|website=Greenpeace New Zealand|language=en-US|access-date=19 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200425033626/https://www.greenpeace.org/new-zealand/campaign/the-green-covid-response-2020/|archive-date=25 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> and the Green Party also put forward their preferences.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.greens.org.nz/greens_push_for_large_intercity_rail_infrastructure_to_ensure_sustainable_post_covid_19_rebuild|title=Greens push for large intercity rail infrastructure to ensure sustainable post-COVID-19 rebuild|last1=Shaw|first1=James|last2=April 19|first2=Julie Anne Genter|website=Green Party of Aotearoa New Zealand|language=en|access-date=19 April 2020|last3=Am|first3=2020 7:40|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200420131515/https://www.greens.org.nz/greens_push_for_large_intercity_rail_infrastructure_to_ensure_sustainable_post_covid_19_rebuild|archive-date=20 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 1 May, the New Zealand Parliament unanimously passed a $23 billion omnibus tax support package. Its provisions include a $3 billion tax relief package for businesses, $25 million for further business support in 2021, a $NZ10 billion wage subsidy scheme, $4.27 billion to support 160,000 small businesses, and $1.3 billion for 8,900 medium-sized businesses.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Walls |first1=Jason |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: MPs unanimously pass biggest tax support package in NZ's history |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12328723 |accessdate=1 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=1 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200501112708/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12328723 |archivedate=1 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=MPs pass biggest tax support package in NZ's history |url=https://www.odt.co.nz/news/national/mps-pass-biggest-tax-support-package-nzs-history |accessdate=1 May 2020 |work=[[Otago Daily Times]] |date=1 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200501113031/https://www.odt.co.nz/news/national/mps-pass-biggest-tax-support-package-nzs-history |archivedate=1 May 2020}}</ref>

=== Local and regional governmental responses ===
On 20 March, the [[Auckland Council]] closed all public libraries, swimming pools, and recreational centres, including the [[Auckland Art Gallery Toi o Tāmaki|Auckland Art Gallery]] and the [[New Zealand Maritime Museum]].<ref>{{cite web |title=Auckland Council to close libraries, pools, recreation centres and major venues |url=https://ourauckland.aucklandcouncil.govt.nz/articles/news/2020/03/auckland-council-to-close-pools-recreation-centres-and-major-venues/ |publisher=[[Auckland Council]] |accessdate=20 March 2020 |date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320004359/https://ourauckland.aucklandcouncil.govt.nz/articles/news/2020/03/auckland-council-to-close-pools-recreation-centres-and-major-venues/ |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Andelane |first1=Lana |title=Coronavirus: Auckland Council to close pools, recreation centres, major venues |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/coronavirus-auckland-council-to-close-pools-recreation-centres-major-venues.html |accessdate=20 March 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320004356/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/coronavirus-auckland-council-to-close-pools-recreation-centres-major-venues.html |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 21 March, several local body councils in Auckland, Wellington, Christchurch, Dunedin, Lower Hutt and Porirua announced the closures of public facilities including swimming pools, libraries, recreation centres, community centres, art galleries, and museums.<ref>{{cite news |title=DCC closes libraries, pools |url=https://www.odt.co.nz/news/dunedin/dcc-closes-libraries-pools?fbclid=IwAR18HwGGiZQjtaGnf3hHX79dC5LJpfiyoj2Pm-eQKTTP_EYnAByhJ3GcceI |accessdate=21 March 2020 |work=[[Otago Daily Times]] |date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321040541/https://www.odt.co.nz/news/dunedin/dcc-closes-libraries-pools%3Ffbclid%3DIwAR18HwGGiZQjtaGnf3hHX79dC5LJpfiyoj2Pm-eQKTTP_EYnAByhJ3GcceI |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite press release |title=Christchurch City Council Closing All Community Facilities |date=21 March 2020 |url=https://www.scoop.co.nz/stories/AK2003/S00368/christchurch-city-council-closing-all-community-facilities.htm |access-date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321041544/https://www.scoop.co.nz/stories/AK2003/S00368/christchurch-city-council-closing-all-community-facilities.htm |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Wellington, Christchurch and Dunedin councils close community facilities |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/wellington-christchurch-and-dunedin-councils-close-community-facilities |accessdate=21 March 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321090124/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/wellington-christchurch-and-dunedin-councils-close-community-facilities |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Councils across New Zealand close facilities indefinitely |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120469553/coronavirus-councils-across-new-zealand-close-facilities-indefinitely |accessdate=22 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321230843/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120469553/coronavirus-councils-across-new-zealand-close-facilities-indefinitely |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 24 March, the Auckland Council announced they were closing their campgrounds and [[Environment Canterbury]] announced that they would also close New Zealand Motor Caravan Association camping grounds within 48 hours.<ref name="NZH lockdown questions" />

Auckland Council announced on 14 April that it was applying for special project funding for a number of infrastructure projects that had been suspended due to lockdown.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Titchall |first1=Alan |title=Councils chase project funding |url=https://localgovernmentmag.co.nz/councils-chase-project-funding/ |publisher=LG: NZ Local Government Magazine |accessdate=15 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415075244/https://localgovernmentmag.co.nz/councils-chase-project-funding/ |archivedate=15 April 2020 |date=14 April 2020}}</ref>

On 15 April, several Otago mayors including [[mayor of Dunedin]] [[Aaron Hawkins (politician)|Aaron Hawkins]], Central Otago District mayor Tim Cadogan, Queenstown Lakes District mayor Jim Boult, Clutha District mayor Bryan Cadogan, Waitaki District mayor Gary Kircher and Otago Regional Council chair [[Marian Hobbs]] were donating part of their salaries to local charities to assist with coronavirus pandemic relief efforts. In addition, several [[Dunedin City Council]] officials including chief executive Sue Bidrose announced that they were taking pay cuts to help their local communities cope with the effects of COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Otago mayors donating 10 per cent of salaries |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/121038266/coronavirus-otago-mayors-donating-10-per-cent-of-salaries |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=15 April 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200415075716/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/121038266/coronavirus-otago-mayors-donating-10-per-cent-of-salaries |archivedate=15 April 2020}}</ref>

On 10 July, the Auckland Council announced that it was going to eliminate 500 permanent jobs as a result of the economic effects of the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Kronast |first1=Hannah |title=Auckland Council to cut over 500 permanent jobs |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/07/auckland-council-to-cut-over-500-permanent-jobs.html |accessdate=10 July 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=10 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200710042700/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/07/auckland-council-to-cut-over-500-permanent-jobs.html |archivedate=10 July 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 27 August, Auckland councillor [[Efeso Collins]] called for the Government to grant an amnesty to people who had overstayed their visas in order to encourage members of the [[Pacific Islander|Pasifika]] community to come forward for COVID-19 tests. The Health Minister Chris Hipkins has reassured the Pasifika community that the Government would not use any information collected during testing for immigration purposes. Collins urged Pacific community leaders, church leaders and health professionals to encourage overstayers to get tested for COVID-19 without fear of repercussions.<ref name="RNZ Pasifika 27 August">{{cite news |title=Auckland councillor Efeso Collins calls for amnesty for people with expired visas |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/covid-19/424564/auckland-councillor-efeso-collins-calls-for-amnesty-for-people-with-expired-visas |accessdate=27 August 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=27 August 2020|url-status=live|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200827073031/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/covid-19/424564/auckland-councillor-efeso-collins-calls-for-amnesty-for-people-with-expired-visas |archivedate=27 August 2020}}</ref>

On 12 November, [[Mayor of Auckland]] [[Phil Goff]] and local health authorities have urged people in the Auckland CBD area to work from home after the discovery of a community transmission case who worked at the A-Z Collections shop on Auckland's High St in the city centre. Goff also criticised the store's owner for allegedly telling the employee to come to work while she was awaiting test results for her COVID-19 test. The store owner disputed Goff's account, explaining that the employee had called on Tuesday to say say she had a sore throat and would be visiting a doctor.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wade |first1=Amelia |title=Covid-19 coronavirus: Auckland CBD staff should work from home if they can, new case's movements revealed |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/politics/covid-19-coronavirus-auckland-cbd-staff-should-work-from-home-if-they-can-new-cases-movements-revealed/V4ITRP35UIGTHGAHMFGNC2AV2I/ |accessdate=12 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=12 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201112090828/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/politics/covid-19-coronavirus-auckland-cbd-staff-should-work-from-home-if-they-can-new-cases-movements-revealed/V4ITRP35UIGTHGAHMFGNC2AV2I/ |archivedate=12 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Block |first1=George |last2=Xia |first2=Lucy |title=Auckland mystery Covid-19 case: Owner of store at centre of controversy speaks |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300157411/auckland-mystery-covid19-case-owner-of-store-at-centre-of-controversy-speaks |accessdate=12 November 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=12 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201112092646/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300157411/auckland-mystery-covid19-case-owner-of-store-at-centre-of-controversy-speaks |archivedate=12 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> The following day, the shop worker issued a statement criticising health officials who interviewed her for not providing a Chinese language translator, causing misinformation about her prior whereabouts, actions, and contacts. As a result of this miscommunication, her employer and their families had received abusive online messages.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 coronavirus: Infected student says health officials made mistakes with her movements |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-infected-student-says-health-officials-made-mistakes-with-her-movements/NAX4JHP2OPBR2WQBGRSTSFGPPI/ |accessdate=13 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=13 November 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201113100342/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-infected-student-says-health-officials-made-mistakes-with-her-movements/NAX4JHP2OPBR2WQBGRSTSFGPPI/|archive-date=13 November 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Block |first1=George |title=Covid-19: Shop employee diagnosed with coronavirus says she never called in sick |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300158205/covid19-shop-employee-diagnosed-with-coronavirus-says-she-never-called-in-sick?cid=app-iPhone |accessdate=13 November 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=13 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201113070820/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300158205/covid19-shop-employee-diagnosed-with-coronavirus-says-she-never-called-in-sick?cid=app-iPhone |archivedate=13 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Repatriation flights and border control===
====New Zealand citizens and residents====
In early February 2020, eleven New Zealanders were reported to be on board the cruise ship ''[[Diamond Princess (ship)|Diamond Princess]]'',<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/02/coronavirus-new-zealanders-quarantined-on-cruise-ship-won-t-be-evacuated-home.html|title=Coronavirus: New Zealanders quarantined on cruise ship won't be evacuated home|date=10 February 2020|work=[[Radio New Zealand]]|access-date=4 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304015244/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/02/coronavirus-new-zealanders-quarantined-on-cruise-ship-won-t-be-evacuated-home.html|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> which had been  quarantined by Japanese authorities in [[Yokohama]] after passengers were confirmed to have COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Bruek|first1=Hilary|url=https://www.businessinsider.com.au/wuhan-coronavirus-photos-inside-diamond-princess-cruise-with-135-sick-2020-2?r=US&IR=T|title=Photos from inside the Diamond Princess cruise ship, where thousands of passengers have been quarantined for a week because of the coronavirus outbreak|date=12 February 2020|work=[[Business Insider|Business Insider Australia]]|access-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200621073015/https://www.businessinsider.com.au/wuhan-coronavirus-photos-inside-diamond-princess-cruise-with-135-sick-2020-2?r=US&IR=T|archive-date=21 June 2020}}</ref> By 20 February, four New Zealand passengers had tested positive for the virus and were being treated in Japan. The remaining six passengers returned to New Zealand via an evacuation flight being organised by the Australian government. Upon arriving in Auckland, they were quarantined at a military facility at [[Whangaparaoa Peninsula|Whangaparaoa]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/409919/coronavirus-two-more-nz-cruise-ship-passengers-test-positive|title=Coronavirus: Two more NZ cruise ship passengers test positive|date=20 February 2020|work=[[Radio New Zealand]]|access-date=4 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304015242/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/409919/coronavirus-two-more-nz-cruise-ship-passengers-test-positive|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

In February 2020, the New Zealand Government used a chartered [[Air New Zealand]] flight to evacuate 193 passengers from Wuhan, China, including 54 New Zealand citizens, 44 permanent residents, 35 Australians, and several Pacific Islands nationals. 35 Australian passengers were transferred to an Australian flight, while the remaining 157 passengers were quarantined in a military facility at Whangaparaoa for 14 days. The passengers were released on 19 February.<ref name="TVNZ mercy flight" /><ref name="Newshub quarantine">{{Cite news|last1=Andelane|first1=Lana|url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/02/coronavirus-157-wuhan-evacuees-permitted-to-leave-quarantine-in-whangaparaoa.html|title=Coronavirus: 157 Wuhan evacuees permitted to leave quarantine in Whangaparaoa|date=19 February 2020|website=[[Newshub]]|access-date=4 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304021051/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/02/coronavirus-157-wuhan-evacuees-permitted-to-leave-quarantine-in-whangaparaoa.html|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 17 March, ''[[Newshub]]'' reported that the [[Australian Border Force]] had suspended the repatriation of New Zealand deportees between 16 and 30 March 2020 as a result of the coronavirus outbreak.<ref>{{cite news |last1=McCann |first1=Mitch |title=Coronavirus: COVID-19 halts Australia's deportation regime |work=[[Newshub]] |date=17 March 2020 |url= https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/coronavirus-covid-19-halts-australia-s-deportation-regime.html |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200317221804/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/coronavirus-covid-19-halts-australia-s-deportation-regime.html |archive-date=17 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 19 March, [[Minister of Foreign Affairs (New Zealand)|Foreign Minister]] [[Winston Peters]] announced that the New Zealand Government was considering more mercy flights to evacuate New Zealanders stranded overseas in response to the spread of the pandemic to Europe, North America and other international locations.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Small |first1=Zane |title=Government planning 'mercy flights' to extract Kiwis stuck overseas |url=https://www.msn.com/en-nz/news/national/government-planning-mercy-flights-to-extract-kiwis-stuck-overseas/ar-BB11o4Vr |accessdate=23 March 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |publisher=[[Microsoft News]] |date=19 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200323081122/https://www.msn.com/en-nz/news/national/government-planning-mercy-flights-to-extract-kiwis-stuck-overseas/ar-BB11o4Vr |archive-date=23 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Government looking into mercy flights for New Zealanders stuck overseas |url=https://www.msn.com/en-nz/news/national/coronavirus-government-looking-into-mercy-flights-for-new-zealanders-stuck-overseas/ar-BB11qtof |accessdate=23 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |publisher=[[Microsoft News]] |date=20 March 2020}}</ref> On 24 March, Prime Minister [[Jacinda Ardern]] urged New Zealanders abroad to return home with while recognising that many will not be able to return home due to the disruption of international travel. Peters urged New Zealanders stranded overseas to considering sheltering "in place". He estimated there were 80,000 New Zealanders stranded overseas, of whom 17,000 had registered with the [[Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Trade (New Zealand)|Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Trade]]'s "Safe Travel" programme.<ref name="Stuff 24 March">{{cite news |last1=Devlin |first1=Collete |title=Coronavirus: Foreign Minister Winston Peters urges New Zealanders abroad to take shelter as PM warns there will be no way home |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120528899/coronavirus-foreign-minister-winston-peters-urges-kiwis-overseas-to-shelter-in-place |accessdate=24 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=24 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324152825/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120528899/coronavirus-foreign-minister-winston-peters-urges-kiwis-overseas-to-shelter-in-place |archivedate=24 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 28 March, it was reported that about 24 New Zealanders were stranded in Peru because they could not board a chartered Australian flight due to changes in Australian transit rules requiring overseas travellers to transit on the same day as their arrival.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Earely |first1=Melanie |title=Coronavirus: New Zealanders stuck in Peru axed from charter flight lifeline |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120653206/coronavirus-new-zealanders-stuck-in-peru-axed-from-charter-flight-lifeline |accessdate=29 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=28 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200329002912/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120653206/coronavirus-new-zealanders-stuck-in-peru-axed-from-charter-flight-lifeline |archivedate=29 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Robson |first1=Sarah |title=Coronavirus: New Zealanders in Peru desperate to return home |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412784/coronavirus-new-zealanders-in-peru-desperate-to-return-home |accessdate=29 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=27 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327230735/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412784/coronavirus-new-zealanders-in-peru-desperate-to-return-home |archivedate=27 March 2020}}</ref>

On 29 March 108 New Zealanders were allowed to disembark from the cruiser liner ''Vasco Da Gama'', which had been berthed at [[Fremantle]], [[Western Australia]], for two weeks. Following the cancellation of the cruise, the passengers had been stranded aboard the cruise ship for two weeks. The passengers were repatriated to Auckland on an Air New Zealand flight.<ref>{{cite news |title=New Zealanders from cruise ship anxious to get home |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412861/new-zealanders-from-cruise-ship-anxious-to-get-home |accessdate=30 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=29 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200329134802/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412861/new-zealanders-from-cruise-ship-anxious-to-get-home |archivedate=29 March 2020}}</ref>

On 30 March, [[Prime Minister of Australia|Australian Prime Minister]] [[Scott Morrison]] announced, following negotiations with Prime Minister Ardern, that New Zealanders in Australia, who held a [[Special Category Visa]], would be eligible for AU$1,500 fortnightly payments as hardship assistance. Many New Zealanders had been forced to return after being unable to access Australian Centrelink payments.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 coronavirus: New Zealanders living in Australia able to access payments |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/news/article.cfm?c_id=2&objectid=12321030 |accessdate=30 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=30 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200330080850/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/news/article.cfm?c_id=2&objectid=12321030 |archivedate=30 March 2020}}</ref>

On 6 April 2020, Peters announced that the Government had organised a mercy flight to rescue New Zealanders stranded in Peru. The flight will depart from [[Lima]], with an added domestic connection in [[Cusco]]. Private tour operators Viva Expeditions and Chimu Adventures will also help transport New Zealanders to the appropriate pickup points. New Zealand authorities have also managed to gain permission from Chilean authorities to transit through [[Santiago]]. According to the [[Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Trade (New Zealand)|Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Trade]], there are 22,000 New Zealanders stranded overseas who have registered with MFAT's Safe Travel.<ref>{{cite news |title=Charter flight to bring stranded Kiwis home from Peru |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413600/charter-flight-to-bring-stranded-kiwis-home-from-peru |accessdate=6 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406113752/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413600/charter-flight-to-bring-stranded-kiwis-home-from-peru |archivedate=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Manch |first1=Thomas |title=Coronavirus: Mercy flight for Kiwis stranded in Peru |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120852237/coronavirus-mercy-flight-for-kiwis-stranded-in-peru |accessdate=6 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=6 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406113946/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120852237/coronavirus-mercy-flight-for-kiwis-stranded-in-peru |archivedate=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 10 April, the Uruguay government announced that it would be repatriating 16 New Zealanders and 96 Australians who had been stranded aboard the Antarctic cruise ship ''Greg Mortimer'' in the [[La Plata river]] near [[Montevideo]] since 27 March. The passengers would be flown from Montevideo to Melbourne.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Kiwis stranded on cruise ship in Uruguay coming home |url= https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12324188 |accessdate=11 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=11 April 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200411100934/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12324188 |archivedate=11 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Regencia |first1=Ted |last2=Stepansky |first2=Joseph |last3=Varshalomidz |first3=Tamila |title=Global coronavirus death toll exceeds 100,000: Live updates |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/04/coronavirus-deaths-rise-signs-progress-live-updates-200409231002574.html |accessdate=11 April 2020 |work=Al Jazeera |date=11 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200411083639/https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/04/coronavirus-deaths-rise-signs-progress-live-updates-200409231002574.html |archive-date=11 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 12 April, the mercy flight carrying 16 New Zealanders landed in Melbourne. Thirteen of the New Zealanders boarded a New Zealand Government-chartered flight to Auckland while three New Zealanders, who were resident in Australia, stayed behind.<ref>{{cite news |title=Mercy flight bringing New Zealand, Aussie cruise ship passengers home |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414051/mercy-flight-bringing-new-zealand-aussie-cruise-ship-passengers-home |accessdate=12 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=12 April 2020 |url-status=live |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200412030229/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414051/mercy-flight-bringing-new-zealand-aussie-cruise-ship-passengers-home |archivedate=12 April 2020}}</ref>

On 15 April, a Government-chartered [[LATAM Airlines Group|LATAM Airlines]] flight carrying New Zealanders who were stranded in Peru arrived back in Auckland. Other passengers who had been scattered in Brazil and Chile were able to board when the flight transited through Santiago. Passengers were to be quarantined in Auckland per new quarantine requirements.<ref>{{cite news |title=Government's Peru repatriation flight arrives in Auckland |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414242/government-s-peru-repatriation-flight-arrives-in-auckland |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=15 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415073312/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414242/government-s-peru-repatriation-flight-arrives-in-auckland |archivedate=15 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="Stuff Kiwis stranded">{{cite news |last1=Earley |first1=Melanie |title=Coronavirus: Kiwis stranded in Peru arrive home on repatriation flight |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/travel-troubles/121014638/coronavirus-kiwis-stranded-in-peru-heading-home-on-repatriation-flight |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=15 April 2020 |url-status=live |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415073738/https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/travel-troubles/121014638/coronavirus-kiwis-stranded-in-peru-heading-home-on-repatriation-flight |archivedate=15 April 2020}}</ref> The mercy flight carried 60 Australians and three New Zealanders. One New Zealand woman elected to stay behind with her Peruvian husband after he failed to meet [[Immigration New Zealand]]'s partnership visa requirements.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Robson |first1=Sarah |title=Couple miss out on coronavirus mercy flight from Peru to NZ after husband declined visa |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/couple-miss-coronavirus-mercy-flight-peru-nz-after-husband-declined-visa |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=15 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415115423/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/couple-miss-coronavirus-mercy-flight-peru-nz-after-husband-declined-visa |archivedate=15 April 2020}}</ref> On 21 April, it was reported that a 49-year-old man, who was meant to be on the Peruvian mercy flight, had died in [[Cusco]] from COVID-19, making him the first New Zealander recorded to have died from it overseas.<ref name="NZ Herald Peru death">{{cite news |last1=Henry |first1=Dubby |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Kiwi, 49, found dead in Peru with Covid-19, family says |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326247 |accessdate=21 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=21 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200421002800/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326247 |archivedate=21 April 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref>

On 15 April, it was announced that [[Fiji Airways]] would be flying stranded New Zealanders from Fiji to Auckland on 17 April. The return flight would leave the same day, carrying Fijians back to [[Nadi]].<ref name="Stuff Kiwis stranded" />

On 13 April, Peters announced that the New Zealand Government was in discussions with airlines and international partners to bring New Zealanders stranded in India back to New Zealand.<ref>{{cite news |title=Government announces repatriation flights for New Zealanders in India |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/414132/government-announces-repatriation-flights-for-new-zealanders-in-india |accessdate=3 May 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=3 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200424204335/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/414132/government-announces-repatriation-flights-for-new-zealanders-in-india |archivedate=24 April 2020}}</ref> On 21 April, Education Minister [[Chris Hipkins]] announced that the Government was repatriating 1,600 New Zealanders from India to managed isolation in Auckland, Wellington, and Christchurch.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Woof |first1=Amber-Leigh |title=Coronavirus: 1600 New Zealanders in India could fly home this week |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/121159633/coronavirus-1600-new-zealanders-in-india-could-fly-home-this-week |accessdate=3 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=21 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200429002502/https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/121159633/coronavirus-1600-new-zealanders-in-india-could-fly-home-this-week |archivedate=29 April 2020}}</ref>

On 21 June, it was reported that 4,272 people who had returned from overseas travel were being housed in 20 managed isolation facilities across New Zealand, including 18 in Auckland and Christchurch and two in [[Rotorua]]. These facilities are being run by the [[National Emergency Management Agency]]. Several returnees complained about lack of communication from ministry officials about their quarantine destinations, including several who had been transferred from Auckland to Rotorua without any prior notice. On 21 June 232 people had returned from Australia and entered into quarantine.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Quarantined travellers angry at being sent to Rotorua with no warning |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12341580 |accessdate=21 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=21 June 2020 |url-status=live |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200621060437/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12341580 |archivedate=21 June 2020}}</ref> That same day, it was reported that a man who had returned from the United Kingdom had been trapped in limbo at Grand Mercure Hotel in Auckland after health authorities lost his COVID-19 test.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Maxwell |first1=Joe |title=Man trapped in 'limbo' under managed isolation after officials lose Covid test |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121894891/man-trapped-in-limbo-under-managed-isolation-after-officials-lose-covid-test |accessdate=21 June 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=21 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200621061032/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121894891/man-trapped-in-limbo-under-managed-isolation-after-officials-lose-covid-test |archivedate=21 June 2020}}</ref>

On 12 July, it was reported that the Government would be establishing a special isolation facility for returning New Zealanders who had been deported from Australia after the Australian Government resumed its deportation policy in late June 2020. According to [[1 News]], 19 New Zealanders are scheduled to return from various Australian detention detentions in the coming week via a chartered flight.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bradford |first1=Katie |title=Special isolation facility being set up in NZ to house Kiwis deported from Australia |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/special-isolation-facility-being-set-up-in-nz-house-kiwis-deported-australia |accessdate=12 July 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=12 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200712102043/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/special-isolation-facility-being-set-up-in-nz-house-kiwis-deported-australia |archivedate=12 July 2020}}</ref> By 28, July at least 30 deportees had arrived from Australia on two chartered flights in July. They were quarantined for 14 days at the Ramada hotel in Auckland.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Block |first1=George |title=Coronavirus: Deported bikie boss released from Auckland isolation |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300067379/coronavirus-deported-bikie-boss-released-from-auckland-isolation |accessdate=28 July 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=28 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200728012754/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300067379/coronavirus-deported-bikie-boss-released-from-auckland-isolation |archivedate=28 July 2020}}</ref>

In September, Sehion Tours and Travels has organised several chartered flights from southern India to Auckland using a [[Singapore Airlines]] [[Airbus A350 XWB#A350-900|A350-900]]. Besides transporting New Zealand citizens and residents, the company is also repatriating Indian nationals who want to return to India.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bradley |first1=Grant |title=Photos: Inside Sehion Tours chartered Singapore Airlines flight from Kochi, India to Auckland |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12364754 |accessdate=15 September 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=14 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Foreign travellers and temporary visa holders====
On 24 March, the New Zealand Government automatically extended all temporary visas with an expiry date of 2 April to 9 July 2020 inclusive who were in New Zealand on 2 April 2020 until 25 September 2020. Travellers whose visas expire before 1 April are allowed to remain if they are unable to leave the country.<ref name="Stuff 24 March" /> On 25 March 2020, the British and German governments announced that they will be sending mercy flights to repatriate stranded citizens in New Zealand, many of whom are tourists. The German government has made arrangements for sending mercy flights to Auckland and Christchurch. The British Government has made arrangements for British nationals to transit through Singapore during their return from New Zealand.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Harris |first1=Dominic |title=Coronavirus: Plans for new flights a lifeline for tourists stranded in NZ |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/120545294/coronavirus-plans-for-new-flights-a-lifeline-for-tourists-stranded-in-nz |accessdate=26 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=25 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326023255/https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/120545294/coronavirus-plans-for-new-flights-a-lifeline-for-tourists-stranded-in-nz |archive-date=26 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> There have been reports of British travellers being charged high airfares by airlines. The British High Commission and consular services in Wellington have been criticised for closing their operations the previous week.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Townsend |first1=Mark |title=Stranded Britons quoted £40,000 each to fly home from New Zealand |url=https://www.theguardian.com/global/2020/mar/28/stranded-britons-quoted-40000-each-to-fly-home-from-new-zealand |accessdate=31 March 2020 |work=[[The Observer]] |date=28 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331023213/https://www.theguardian.com/global/2020/mar/28/stranded-britons-quoted-40000-each-to-fly-home-from-new-zealand |archive-date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Harris |first1=Dominic |title=Coronavirus: Trapped tourists 'swindled' by airlines' ticket prices and voucher refunds |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/travel-troubles/120615282/coronavirus-trapped-tourists-swindled-by-airlines-ticket-prices-and-voucher-refunds |accessdate=31 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=28 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328192833/https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/travel-troubles/120615282/coronavirus-trapped-tourists-swindled-by-airlines-ticket-prices-and-voucher-refunds |archive-date=28 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 31 March, Malaysian Deputy Foreign Minister [[Kamaruddin Jaffar]] stated that 153 Malaysians with return tickets were stranded in New Zealand but unable to return to Malaysia due to travel restrictions and disruption caused by the pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Mohsen |first1=Amar |title=More than 4,300 M'sians still stranded overseas, says deputy minister |url=https://www.thesundaily.my/local/more-than-4300-m-sians-still-stranded-overseas-says-deputy-minister-YY2199427#pk_campaign=MASwpn&pk_kwd=More+than+4%2C300+M%E2%80%99sians+still+stranded+overseas%2C+says+deputy+minister |accessdate=31 March 2020 |work=[[The Sun (Malaysia)|The Sun]] |date=31 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405164615/https://www.thesundaily.my/local/more-than-4300-m-sians-still-stranded-overseas-says-deputy-minister-YY2199427#pk_campaign=MASwpn&pk_kwd=More+than+4%2C300+M%E2%80%99sians+still+stranded+overseas%2C+says+deputy+minister |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

In early April, Deputy Prime Minister [[Winston Peters]], following communications with foreign governments including Denmark,<ref>{{cite news |last1=Tuckey |first1=Karoline |title=Overseas travellers relieved to be heading home |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413435/overseas-travellers-relieved-to-be-heading-home |accessdate=5 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=4 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200404043135/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413435/overseas-travellers-relieved-to-be-heading-home |archivedate=4 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> announced that foreign nationals returning home would be classified as engaging in essential travel able to travel domestically (whether by air or land) when they have a confirmed and scheduled international flight out of New Zealand, subject to Government requirements. In addition, foreign governments would be allowed to evacuate their citizens in charter flights provided they satisfied New Zealand health requirements. To improve travel between New Zealand and Europe, the Government has also approved a second daily flight between [[Doha]] to Auckland by [[Qatar Airways]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Stranded foreigners to start leaving NZ tomorrow |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12319663 |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=2 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402032013/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12319663 |archivedate=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Molyneux |first1=Vita |title=Tens of thousands of stranded tourists will be helped out of New Zealand despite coronavirus lockdown |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/04/tens-of-thousands-of-stranded-tourists-to-be-removed-from-new-zealand-despite-coronavirus-lockdown.html |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=2 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402032153/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/04/tens-of-thousands-of-stranded-tourists-to-be-removed-from-new-zealand-despite-coronavirus-lockdown.html |archivedate=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

As of 10 April, German airliner [[Lufthansa]] has flown 16 repatriation flights from [[Auckland International Airport]] to Germany, Switzerland, and Austria, evacuating 6,700 passengers.<ref>{{cite news |title=Kiwis who helped stranded German travellers thanked with Auckland flyover by Lufthansa |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/kiwis-helped-stranded-german-travellers-thanked-auckland-flyover-lufthansa?auto=6148487279001 |accessdate=10 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=10 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200410041939/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/kiwis-helped-stranded-german-travellers-thanked-auckland-flyover-lufthansa?auto=6148487279001 |archivedate=10 April 2020}}</ref> On 14 April, it was reported that [[Qatar Airways]] would be flying a [[Boeing 777-300]] via Perth to pick up stranded French nationals in Christchurch before returning to Paris.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bradley |first1=Grant |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Qatar Airways flying Christchurch to Paris |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12324715 |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=14 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200414124931/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12324715 |archivedate=14 April 2020}}</ref>

On 13 May, Deputy Prime Minister Winston Peters urged migrant workers who were out of work to go home, stating that New Zealand taxpayers could not afford to support them. Peters confirmed that 50,000 migrant workers had already returned to their home countries after the New Zealand Government made arrangements with embassies to organise repatriation flights for their nationals. According to a declassified official document, there were over 383,000 foreign nationals in New Zealand including students, migrant workers, and partners or dependents of workers as of 30 March.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wade |first1=Amelia |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Winston Peters tells struggling migrant workers 'you should probably go home' |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12331405 |accessdate=15 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=13 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200515110635/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12331405 |archivedate=15 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=COVID-19: All of Government Plan for Managing Stranded People |url=https://covid19.govt.nz/assets/resources/proactive-release/COVID-19_-All-of-Government-Plan-for-Managing-Stranded-People-Paper.pdf |website=Covid19.govt.nz |publisher=[[New Zealand Government]] |accessdate=15 May 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200515093542/https://covid19.govt.nz/assets/resources/proactive-release/COVID-19_-All-of-Government-Plan-for-Managing-Stranded-People-Paper.pdf |archive-date=15 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

According to a [[1 News]] report on 17 May, there are over 1,000 [[Recognised Seasonal Employer scheme]] workers in New Zealand, mostly from the Pacific Islands. Pacific Response Coordination Team chairman Pakilau Manase Lua has stated that about 1,000 Tongan seasonal workers in NZ are facing financial difficulty due to the loss of work caused by the economic upheaval caused by the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Dreaver |first1=Barbara |title=Calls for Pacific and NZ Governments to work together to get stranded seasonal workers home |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/calls-pacific-and-nz-governments-work-together-get-stranded-seasonal-workers-home |accessdate=17 May 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=17 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200517222131/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/calls-pacific-and-nz-governments-work-together-get-stranded-seasonal-workers-home |archivedate=17 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 3 June, [[Radio New Zealand]] reported that half of the Government's $30 million emergency welfare fund had been spent over a month, with many of the recipients including stranded migrant workers and foreigners who were unable to return to their countries due to the disruption of international travel. Under the Civil Defence Emergency Management Act, financial assistance for food, transport, clothing and accommodation is available to anyone regardless of their citizenship. Civil Defence Minister [[Peeni Henare]] has confirmed that there have been 4,500 requests for emergency assistance from the [[Otago]] region with an unknown number from the [[Auckland Region]]. Immigration Minister [[Iain Lees-Galloway]] has stated that the "labour market test" will be applied on foreign workers once their work visas have expired.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Moir |first1=Jo |title=Govt's emergency welfare fund depletes with foreigners still stranded |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/418124/govt-s-emergency-welfare-fund-depletes-with-foreigners-still-stranded |accessdate=2 June 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602230852/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/418124/govt-s-emergency-welfare-fund-depletes-with-foreigners-still-stranded |archivedate=2 June 2020}}</ref>

On 7 July, the Immigration Minister Iain Lees-Galloway extended 16,500 Essential Skills and Work to Residence workers with visas by six months and extended the 12-month stand-down period for migrant workers who were going to leave in 2020 until February 2021. This stand-down period shift would benefit about 600 lower-skilled visa holders including dairy workers.<ref>{{cite news |title=Government extends temporary work visas by six months |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/420688/government-extends-temporary-work-visas-by-six-months |accessdate=7 July 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=7 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200707101331/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/420688/government-extends-temporary-work-visas-by-six-months |archivedate=7 July 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 10 July, the Government announced that overseas-based victims of the [[Christchurch mosque shootings]] would be granted special border passes and financial help in order to travel to New Zealand for the duration of the gunman's sentencing, which begins on 24 August.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bayer |first1=Kurt |title=Christchurch mosque shooting: Border exceptions for victims based overseas to attend gunman's sentencing |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12347157 |accessdate=10 July 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=10 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200710040509/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12347157 |archivedate=10 July 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 22 July, [[Radio New Zealand]] reported that a six year old Korean child had been unable to attend school since his father, a temporary visa holder, was unable to return to New Zealand due to lockdown travel restrictions. Under New Zealand law, international students under the age of ten are unable to attend schools without the presence of a parent or guardian. Despite lobbying by National MP [[Melissa Lee]] on behalf of the family, Education Minister Chris Hipkins declined to intervene, citing policy issues.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Scotcher |first1=Katie |title=Covid-19 border restrictions leave Korean boy stranded in NZ and unable to go to school |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/421733/covid-19-border-restrictions-leave-korean-boy-stranded-in-nz-and-unable-to-go-to-school |accessdate=3 August 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=22 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200723072502/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/421733/covid-19-border-restrictions-leave-korean-boy-stranded-in-nz-and-unable-to-go-to-school|archive-date=23 July 2020}}</ref>

On 9 September, the Government announced that it would be increasing the number of categories of non-citizens and non-residents eligible for the new border exception. These include those holding a job or operating a business in New Zealand; holding a work to residence or essential skills visa, have departed New Zealand on or after 1 December 2019; and have lived in New Zealand for at least two years with a residence or work visa. Partners who are Australian citizens or from visa-waiver countries will also be eligible to apply for border exceptions. In addition, those who have been unable to enter the country to activate their residency visa or unable to return before their residency visa expires will receive a reprieve.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Government announces new border exemptions, changes to resident visas |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-government-announces-new-border-exemptions-changes-to-resident-visas.html |accessdate=9 September 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=9 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200909084700/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-government-announces-new-border-exemptions-changes-to-resident-visas.html |archivedate=9 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

By 12 October, it was reported that 10,400 individuals had been granted exemptions for critical and essential work to enter New Zealand.<ref name="1 News border exemption 12 Oct 2020" />

On 13 November, it was reported that Prime Minister Ardern had granted a business exemption for a British family to enter New Zealand following the death of their son Eddie in French Polynesia in April 2020.  The family had initially been denied entry into New Zealand but the Prime Minister had sought a review of the case after the ''Weekend Herald'' reported on the family's situation on 10 October.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Dillane |first1=Tom |title=UK family whose son died at sea praise Jacinda Ardern for New Zealand entry decision reversal |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/uk-family-whose-son-died-at-sea-praise-jacinda-ardern-for-new-zealand-entry-decision-reversal/MLWWVWAOPZELHOJJT2N2ZGJ64A/ |accessdate=13 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=13 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201113081423/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/uk-family-whose-son-died-at-sea-praise-jacinda-ardern-for-new-zealand-entry-decision-reversal/MLWWVWAOPZELHOJJT2N2ZGJ64A/ |archivedate=13 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Health sector responses===
On 19 March, the medical recruitment company MedWorld appealed for retired and part-time doctors to assist efforts by the health sector and Government to combat the spread of COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Russell |first1=Emma |title=Coronavirus: Urgent calls for retired doctors and nurses to step up |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318535 |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=19 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324210936/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318535 |archivedate=24 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=McKenzie-McLean |first1=Jo |title=Coronavirus: 'Call to Arms' for retired doctors and nurses to help hospitals fight infection |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120441250/coronavirus-call-to-arms-for-retired-doctors-and-nurses-to-help-hospitals-fight-infection |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=19 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321173211/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120441250/coronavirus-call-to-arms-for-retired-doctors-and-nurses-to-help-hospitals-fight-infection |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 10 June, [[St John New Zealand]], which provides ambulance and first aid services, announced that it would be laying off staff due to a $30 million deficit caused by the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: St John facing staff cuts, aims to save $30 million |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12338877 |accessdate=11 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=10 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200610155212/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12338877 |archivedate=11 June 2020}}</ref> The organisation had also tried to apply for the Government's wage subsidy scheme but was told that it was not eligible for it despite a 40% drop in income.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Macfarlane |first1=Andrew |title=Jobs will be lost as St John Ambulance looks to slash $30m due to Covid-19, CEO says in memo |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/jobs-lost-st-john-ambulance-looks-slash-30m-due-covid-19-ceo-says-in-memo |accessdate=11 June 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=10 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200611002906/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/jobs-lost-st-john-ambulance-looks-slash-30m-due-covid-19-ceo-says-in-memo |archivedate=11 June 2020}}</ref>

On 27 August, Pasifika GP Network member Dr Api Talemaitoga announced that the Government's Testing Strategy Group would seek to ensure that members of the [[Māori people|Māori]] and [[Pacific Islander|Pasifika]] communities would have fair access to testing. These measures include offering free testing, mobile testing centers and clinicians who could translate. Health authorities have also sought to reassure members of these communities that they would not lose their jobs due to contracting COVID-19.<ref name="RNZ Pasifika 27 August" />

===Business sector responses===

Up until March 2020, New Zealand ran a [[mixed economy]] – a [[free market]] with some [[Public sector organisations in New Zealand|state ownership and control]].<ref>

On 17 September 2020, New Zealand economy officially entered into a recession, with the country's gross domestic product contracting by 12.2% in the June quarter due to the COVID-19 pandemic. The retail, accommodation, hospitality, and transportation sectors were adversely affected by the international travel ban and a strict nationwide lockdown.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19: GDP results show NZ officially in first recession in a decade |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/426270/covid-19-gdp-results-show-nz-officially-in-first-recession-in-a-decade |accessdate=17 September 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=17 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200917051201/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/426270/covid-19-gdp-results-show-nz-officially-in-first-recession-in-a-decade |archivedate=17 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Pullar-Strecker |first1=Tom |title=NZ in recession as Covid shrinks GDP by 12.2% |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122796028/nz-in-recession-as-covid-shrinks-gdp-by-122 |accessdate=17 September 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=17 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200917001110/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122796028/nz-in-recession-as-covid-shrinks-gdp-by-122 |archivedate=17 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Roy |first1=Eleanor |title=New Zealand in Covid recession after worst quarterly GDP fall on record |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/sep/17/new-zealand-in-covid-recession-after-worst-quarterly-gdp-fall-on-record |accessdate=17 September 2020 |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=16 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200917043007/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/sep/17/new-zealand-in-covid-recession-after-worst-quarterly-gdp-fall-on-record |archivedate=17 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Agriculture====
On 31 March 2020, NZ Pork CEO David Baines warned that the Government's decision to classify butcheries as non-essential services would have serious implications for the welfare pigs on New Zealand farms. Due to a surplus in pigs, many farms lacked sufficient space to store pigs.<ref>{{cite news |title=Concerns for welfare of surplus pigs as butchers around NZ ordered to close |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/concerns-welfare-surplus-pigs-butchers-around-nz-ordered-close |accessdate=20 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=31 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200420091758/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/concerns-welfare-surplus-pigs-butchers-around-nz-ordered-close|archivedate=20 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Skerrett |first1=Angie |title=Coronavirus: Exclusion of butchers as essential service will cause 'animal welfare crisis' says pork sector |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/rural/2020/03/coronavirus-exclusion-of-butchers-as-essential-service-will-cause-animal-welfare-crisis-says-pork-sector.html |accessdate=20 April 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=31 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403211033/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/rural/2020/03/coronavirus-exclusion-of-butchers-as-essential-service-will-cause-animal-welfare-crisis-says-pork-sector.html |archivedate=3 April 2020}}</ref>

On 22 August, it was reported that about 2.5 million bees had starved to death after workers from Waikato were unable to travel to Auckland to access beehives due to checkpoints imposed following a surge in community transmissions in Auckland. Businesses affected include Waitakaruru Honey Limited. Apiculture New Zealand had applied to the Ministry of Health for an exemption on behalf of commercial bee keepers.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Fyfe |first1=James |title=Coronavirus: Millions of bees starve to death as beekeepers held up at COVID-19 checkpoints |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/rural/2020/08/coronavirus-millions-of-bees-starve-to-death-as-beekeepers-held-up-at-covid-19-checkpoints.html |accessdate=21 August 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=21 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200821121817/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/rural/2020/08/coronavirus-millions-of-bees-starve-to-death-as-beekeepers-held-up-at-covid-19-checkpoints.html |archivedate=21 August 2020}}</ref>

In October and November 2020, the horticultural and viticultural industries reported a shortage of workers since the Government's border restrictions and managed isolation requirements prevented tourists and seasonal workers from entering the country. Under the [[Recognised Seasonal Employer]] scheme, horticultural and viticultural producers are normally allowed to recruit seasonal workers from the [[Pacific Islands]] and selected Asian countries. In addition, tourists from certain countries are allowed to work on a visitor visa. This labour shortage has caused fruits and crops to rot. Local growers have reported difficulty in recruiting locals due to the long hours, hard, outdoor work, lower wages, and them lacking the specialised picking and plant-care skills that foreign workers.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Fisher |first1=David |title=Fields of courgettes go to waste because grower can't get workers |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/fields-of-courgettes-go-to-waste-because-grower-cant-get-workers/WU663T7JRQVDDOYTBOXMA4VPIY/ |access-date=23 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=7 November 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201120030035/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/fields-of-courgettes-go-to-waste-because-grower-cant-get-workers/WU663T7JRQVDDOYTBOXMA4VPIY/|archive-date=20 November 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Immigration Minister says allowing fruit pickers into NZ to fix labour shortage 'not an option' |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/rural/2020/10/immigration-minister-says-allowing-fruit-pickers-into-nz-to-fix-labour-shortage-not-an-option.html |access-date=23 November 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=7 October 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201017105614/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/rural/2020/10/immigration-minister-says-allowing-fruit-pickers-into-nz-to-fix-labour-shortage-not-an-option.html|archive-date=17 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Hall |first1=Kristin |title=Kiwi fruit pickers have simple message as growers cry out for labour – 'pay us more' |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/kiwi-fruit-pickers-have-simple-message-growers-cry-labour-pay-us-more |access-date=23 November 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=7 November 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/kiwi-fruit-pickers-have-simple-message-growers-cry-labour-pay-us-more|archive-date=17 November 2020}}</ref><ref name="Stuff Horticulture work really hard">{{cite news |last1=Stock |first1=Rob |title=Horticulture work 'really hard' at first, but there's decent money to be made |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/123203930/horticulture-work-really-hard-at-first-but-theres-decent-money-to-be-made |access-date=23 November 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=29 October 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201104000101/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/123203930/horticulture-work-really-hard-at-first-but-theres-decent-money-to-be-made|archive-date=4 November 2020}}</ref>

In mid&ndash;October 2020 Richard Palmer, the CEO of the producer representative body Summerfruit New Zealand, warned that the horticulture might not be able to pick up 30% of its harvest that year, a shortfall that could cost NZ$1.25 billion in export earnings.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Dunkley |first1=David |title=Fruit-picking jobs going begging: Who is really to blame? |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/opinion-analysis/300138256/fruitpicking-jobs-going-begging-who-is-really-to-blame |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |agency=24 November 2020 |date=22 October 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201119075115/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/opinion-analysis/300138256/fruitpicking-jobs-going-begging-who-is-really-to-blame |archive-date=19 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> In late October 2020, Horticulture NZ and the New Zealand Apples and Pears Inc launched a jobs service called Pick Tiki to recruit urban young people into fruit-picking jobs in [[Hawke's Bay Region|Hawke's Bay]], [[Nelson, New Zealand|Nelson]], and [[Central Otago]].<ref name="Stuff Horticulture work really hard" />

====Aviation====
On 16 March, the national carrier [[Air New Zealand]] announced that it would be reducing its long-haul capacity by 85% and its personnel by 30% in response to declining demand and revenue as a result of the outbreak. In addition to the previously suspended flights to [[Shanghai Pudong International Airport|Shanghai]] and [[Incheon International Airport|Seoul]], the airline suspended flights to several major international cities including [[San Francisco International Airport|San Francisco]], [[George Bush Intercontinental Airport|Houston]], [[Ministro Pistarini International Airport|Buenos Aires]], [[Vancouver International Airport|Vancouver]], [[Narita International Airport|Tokyo]], [[Daniel K. Inouye International Airport|Honolulu]], [[Ngurah Rai International Airport|Denpasar]], and [[Taoyuan International Airport|Taipei]] between 30 March and 30 June as well as its [[Heathrow Airport|London Heathrow]]–[[Los Angeles International Airport|Los Angeles]] service. The airline also reduced trans-Tasman capacity by 80%, and the domestic network capacity would be reduced in March and April 2020. It would maintain enough overseas flights for returning New Zealanders and evacuees as well as essential air freight.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pelletier |first1=Nona |title=Coronavirus: Air NZ halts share trading, slashes long-haul flights |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/covid-19/411826/coronavirus-air-nz-halts-share-trading-slashes-long-haul-flights |accessdate=16 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=16 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317133516/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/covid-19/411826/coronavirus-air-nz-halts-share-trading-slashes-long-haul-flights |archive-date=17 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Edmunds |first1=Susan |title=Air New Zealand cuts long-haul capacity by 85 per cent, 'dropping 30% of staff' |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Air New Zealand to keep flying with Government's almost $1 billion rescue package
