|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319205814/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/air-new-zealand-keep-flying-governments-almost-1-billion-rescue-package |archive-date=19 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 19 March, it was reported that [[Qantas]] and [[Jetstar]] were suspending their New Zealand operations as part of their efforts to suspend international flights in response to the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Anthony |first1=John |title=Coronavirus: All Qantas and Jetstar international flights suspended from late March |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120403628/coronavirus-all-qantas-and-jetstar-international-flights-suspended-from-late-march |accessdate=29 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=19 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331223346/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120403628/coronavirus-all-qantas-and-jetstar-international-flights-suspended-from-late-march |archive-date=31 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 25 March, Air New Zealand's chief revenue officer announced the airline would cut back to just ten international and fifth-freedom routes from 30 March to 1 May: from [[Auckland Airport|Auckland]] to [[Sydney Airport|Sydney]], [[Brisbane Airport|Brisbane]], [[Melbourne Airport|Melbourne]], [[Rarotonga International Airport|Rarotonga]], [[Nadi International Airport|Nadi]], [[Niue International Airport|Niue]], Los Angeles and [[Hong Kong International Airport|Hong Kong]], and from [[Norfolk Island Airport|Norfolk Island]] to Sydney and Brisbane. The Auckland to Shanghai route would resume on 2 May.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12319910|title=Covid-19 coronavirus: Air New Zealand drops international flights to just 11 routes|date=25 March 2020|work=[[The New Zealand Herald]]|access-date=25 March 2020|language=en-NZ|issn=1170-0777|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325103506/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12319910|archive-date=25 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 4 April, it became known that [[Virgin Australia]] had decided to shut down its New Zealand operation permanently, resulting in 600 jobs in New Zealand to be lost.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Palmer |first1=Scott |title=Union 'hugely disappointed' Virgin Australia axing New Zealand bases |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/travel/2020/04/union-hugely-disappointed-virgin-australia-axing-new-zealand-bases.html |accessdate=4 April 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=4 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406155924/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/travel/2020/04/union-hugely-disappointed-virgin-australia-axing-new-zealand-bases.html |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 7 April, it was reported that Air New Zealand was considering laying off 387 pilots as part of cutback measures. The New Zealand Air Line Pilots' Association (NZALPA), which represents 1520 Air New Zealand pilots, is currently in negotiations with the airline to reduce the number of layoffs.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Anthony |first1=John |last2=Carroll |first2=Melanie |title=Coronavirus: Air New Zealand proposes to make 387 pilots redundant, union says |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/120863685/coronavirus-air-new-zealand-begins-pilot-redundancies |accessdate=7 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=7 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407053748/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/120863685/coronavirus-air-new-zealand-begins-pilot-redundancies |archivedate=7 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 20 May, Air New Zealand announced that it would be laying off 3,500 personnel.<ref>{{cite news |title=Air New Zealand announces 3500 job losses due to Covid-19 pandemic |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/air-new-zealand-announces-3500-job-losses-due-covid-19-pandemic |accessdate=20 May 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=20 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200520074838/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/air-new-zealand-announces-3500-job-losses-due-covid-19-pandemic |archivedate=20 May 2020}}</ref> This includes 1,300 cabin crew. 950 long and mid-haul crew will lose their jobs while 300 workers will be made redundant in Auckland, Wellington, and Christchurch. In addition, 97 jobs were lost at Air NZ's regional airlines [[Air Nelson]] and [[Mount Cook Airline]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bradley |first1=Grant |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Air NZ – more than 1300 staff to lose jobs: union |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12333373 |accessdate=20 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=20 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200520074621/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12333373|archive-date=20 May 2020}}</ref>

In early June, [[Singapore Airlines]] announced that it would resume passenger flights to Auckland and Christchurch on a weekly basis.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Singapore Airlines to resume New Zealand services |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/news/121692522/coronavirus-singapore-airlines-to-resume-new-zealand-services |accessdate=2 June 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=2 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602030400/https://www.stuff.co.nz/travel/news/121692522/coronavirus-singapore-airlines-to-resume-new-zealand-services |archivedate=2 June 2020}}</ref> On 10 June, it was reported that Singapore Airlines staff were being quarantined in hotel rooms for the duration of their three-day stay.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Tan |first1=Lincoln |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Singapore Airlines crew 'kept like prisoners' during NZ layover |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12338813 |accessdate=11 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200610155108/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12338813 |archivedate=10 June 2020}}</ref> In mid-June, Air New Zealand announced that it would be resuming flights between Auckland and Shanghai from 22 June.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Lake |first1=Dan |title=Air New Zealand to resume Auckland-Shanghai service on June 22 |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/travel/2020/06/air-new-zealand-to-resume-auckland-shanghai-service-on-june-22.html |accessdate=16 June 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=16 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200616072707/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/travel/2020/06/air-new-zealand-to-resume-auckland-shanghai-service-on-june-22.html |archivedate=16 June 2020}}</ref>

On 5 July, Air New Zealand attracted criticism after it removed 11 passengers from an overcrowded flight to [[Brisbane]] and erroneously told them that they would have to pay for their accommodation, meals and other quarantine costs until the next flight was ready to depart on Tuesday. Police were called to mediate between airline staff and passengers. Air New Zealand subsequently apologised for providing the passengers with incorrect information.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Orsman |first1=Bernard |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Hysterical scenes as passengers in Auckland taken off plane to quarantine |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12345607 |accessdate=5 July 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=5 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200705113612/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12345607 |archivedate=5 July 2020}}</ref>

On 3 August, [[Auckland International Airport]] announced that it would be splitting its international terminal into separate zones for travellers from "safe travel hubs" and "health management" areas in anticipation for the establishment of a safe air corridor between New Zealand and the [[Cook Islands]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 coronavirus: Auckland International Airport to be split into two zones |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12353350 |accessdate=3 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=3 August 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200803113545/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12353350|archive-date=3 August 2020}}</ref>

On 12 August, following several recent community transmissions, it was announced that all passengers leaving Auckland Airport would be issued with masks while passengers entering Auckland would be required to wear masks. Access to Auckland Airport would be limited to those with valid tickets, travel itineraries and traveling overseas. Social distancing would also be re-introduced at airports across the country.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 travel restrictions: Masks on flights as measures take effect |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/423355/covid-19-travel-restrictions-masks-on-flights-as-measures-take-effect |accessdate=12 August 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=12 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200812033022/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/423355/covid-19-travel-restrictions-masks-on-flights-as-measures-take-effect |archivedate=12 August 2020}}</ref>

On 15 August, Jetstar suspended its domestic operations in New Zealand after the Government implemented social distancing rules following a second outbreak in Auckland that month.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Jetstar pauses all domestic flights until August 26 |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12356805 |accessdate=14 September 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=15 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200816014243/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12356805 |archivedate=16 August 2020}}</ref>

On 14 September, Jetstar announced that it was resuming domestic flights in New Zealand after Prime Minister Ardern announced that physical distancing on aircraft was no longer required. The airline had suspended its domestic services in New Zealand four weeks earlier following an outbreak in Auckland in mid-August 2020.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Taunton |first1=Esther |title=Jetstar to resume domestic flights after four-week suspension |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122760021/jetstar-to-resume-domestic-flights-after-fourweek-suspension |accessdate=14 September 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=14 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200914041445/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122760021/jetstar-to-resume-domestic-flights-after-fourweek-suspension |archivedate=14 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Cafes and restaurants====
On 14 April, it was reported that three parent shareholding companies of the [[Burger King]] franchise in New Zealand had gone into receivership, with [[KordaMentha]] appointed as receiver. It was hoped that Burger King would start trading again post-lockdown as its operating company was not in receivership.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Carroll |first1=Melanie |title=Coronavirus: Burger King NZ owners in receivership, hopes of sale |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/121000806/burger-king-franchise-owner-in-receivership |accessdate=14 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=14 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200414100842/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/121000806/burger-king-franchise-owner-in-receivership |archive-date=14 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

====Camping grounds====
On 24 March, two local authorities and the [[New Zealand Motor Caravan Association]] announced that they were closing their camping grounds.<ref name="NZH lockdown questions" />

====Casinos====
On 11 May, [[Skycity Entertainment Group|Skycity]] announced that it will be slashing 700 jobs as a result of the economic fallout of the pandemic. In April, the company had slashed 200 jobs.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Flaws |first1=Bonnie |title=Coronavirus: Sky City announces more job losses to come |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121471401/coronavirus-sky-city-announces-more-job-losses-to-come |accessdate=12 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=11 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200511235611/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121471401/coronavirus-sky-city-announces-more-job-losses-to-come |archivedate=11 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=SkyCity plans 700 job cuts due to Covid-19 downturn |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/416344/skycity-plans-700-job-cuts-due-to-covid-19-downturn |accessdate=12 May 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=11 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512000146/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/416344/skycity-plans-700-job-cuts-due-to-covid-19-downturn |archivedate=12 May 2020}}</ref>

====Construction sector====
On 28 April 2020, it became known that steel company [[Steel & Tube Holdings Limited|Steel & Tube]] would lose between 150 and 200 jobs in upcoming restructuring.<ref>{{cite news |title=Steel and Tube to make up to 200 staff redundant |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/415287/steel-and-tube-to-make-up-to-200-staff-redundant |accessdate=28 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=28 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200501050301/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/415287/steel-and-tube-to-make-up-to-200-staff-redundant |archive-date=1 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 20 May, building company [[Fletcher Building]] announced that they would be laying off at least 1,000 jobs in New Zealand and 500 jobs in Australia, amounting to ten percent of their workforce.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bradford |first1=Katie |title=About 1000 NZ jobs to vanish as Fletcher Building announces massive redundancy plan |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/fletcher-building-lay-off-10-workforce-1000-jobs-in-nz |accessdate=20 May 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=20 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200520073441/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/fletcher-building-lay-off-10-workforce-1000-jobs-in-nz |archivedate=20 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Nadkarni |first1=Anuja |title=Coronavirus: Fletcher Building job cuts paint grim picture of economy, analyst says |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121555737/coronavirus-fletcher-building-job-cuts-paint-grim-picture-of-economy-analyst-says |accessdate=20 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=20 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200520073720/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121555737/coronavirus-fletcher-building-job-cuts-paint-grim-picture-of-economy-analyst-says |archivedate=20 May 2020}}</ref> On 11 August, it was reported that Fletcher Building was expecting a loss of NZ$196 million for the year to June 2020 due to the pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Nadkarni |first1=Anuja |title=Fletcher Building expects $196m net loss because of Covid-19 |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300079155/fletcher-building-expects-196m-net-loss-because-of-covid19 |accessdate=11 August 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=11 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200819181038/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300079155/fletcher-building-expects-196m-net-loss-because-of-covid19 |archivedate=11 August 2020}}</ref>

====Film industry====
On 17 March, [[Jon Landau (film producer)|Jon Landau]], the co-producer of the ''[[Avatar (2009 film)|Avatar]]'' [[Avatar 2|film]] [[Avatar 3|sequels]], announced that film production at the Wellington-based Stone Street Studios had been suspended in response to the pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Dillane |first1=Tom |title=Coronavirus in NZ: James Cameron's Avatar filming delayed indefinitely |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/entertainment/news/article.cfm?c_id=1501119&objectid=12317556 |accessdate=17 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=17 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317120704/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/entertainment/news/article.cfm?c_id=1501119&objectid=12317556 |archive-date=17 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> However, visual effects will continue at [[Weta Digital]] in Wellington.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Landau |first1=Jon |title=Production of Avatar sequels delayed; visual effects work continues at Weta Digital |url=http://wellington.scoop.co.nz/?p=126634 |accessdate=28 March 2020 |work=[[Scoop (website)|Scoop]] |date=19 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200319233204/http://wellington.scoop.co.nz/?p=126634 |archivedate=19 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 31 May 50 ''Avatar'' crew including Hollywood director [[James Cameron]] were granted entry into New Zealand under a special visa category for border exemptions for foreigners deemed essential to a project of "significant economic value."<ref>{{cite news |title=Avatar crew touch down in Wellington |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12336159 |accessdate=2 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=31 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602105559/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12336159 |archivedate=2 July 2020}}</ref>

====Financial services====
On 1 July, [[ASB Bank]] announced that they were closing nine branches in the major centres and that 25 branches will be moving to three day weeks due to a shift in demand for online services. Branches that will be closing are at [[Auckland Hospital]], [[Parnell, New Zealand|Parnell]], Ronwood Avenue in [[Manukau City]], [[Ellerslie, New Zealand|Ellerslie]] and [[Mount Albert, New Zealand|Mount Albert]] in [[Auckland]], [[Waikato University]] in [[Hamilton, New Zealand|Hamilton]], [[Papamoa]] in [[Bay of Plenty]], [[Barrington, New Zealand|Barrington]] in [[Christchurch]] and [[Mosgiel]] in [[Otago]].<ref name="RNZ ASB">{{cite news |title=Nine ASB branches to close, 25 others to have opening hours slashed |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/420242/nine-asb-branches-to-close-25-others-to-have-opening-hours-slashed |accessdate=1 July 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=1 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200701081616/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/420242/nine-asb-branches-to-close-25-others-to-have-opening-hours-slashed|archive-date=1 July 2020}}</ref><ref name="Newshub ASB">{{cite news |last1=Burrows |first1=Matt |title=ASB Bank closing nine branches in New Zealand's main centres |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/money/2020/07/asb-bank-losing-nine-branches-in-new-zealand-s-main-centres.html |accessdate=1 July 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=1 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200701081933/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/money/2020/07/asb-bank-losing-nine-branches-in-new-zealand-s-main-centres.html |archivedate=1 July 2020}}</ref> The company will also hire 150 additional staff to provide specialist online support.<ref name="Newshub ASB" />

On 19 November, the [[Bank of New Zealand]] announced that it was closing 38 branches over the next seven months as a result of the economic effects of the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Edmonds |first1=Susan |title=BNZ to close 38 bank branches |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300162532/bnz-to-close-38-bank-branches?cid=app-iPhone |accessdate=19 November 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=19 November 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201119035232/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300162532/bnz-to-close-38-bank-branches|archive-date=19 November 2020}}</ref>

====Funeral services====
Funeral directors have warned about a spike in violence as a result of people being unable to attend funerals for their loved ones during the Level 4 and Level 3 restrictions.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Russell |first1=Emma |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Funeral directors warn rise of violence due to people being unable to grieve |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12330067 |accessdate=7 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=6 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200507051920/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12330067 |archivedate=7 May 2020}}</ref>

====Maritime sector====
In early June, marine engineering company Airmex's managing director Steve Sullivan has warned that about 40 jobs maritime engineering jobs in Nelson are at risk due to the Government's policy of refusing entry to ships as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic. According to Sullivan, 40% of the company's revenue came from the international refit business. National MP [[Nick Smith (New Zealand politician)|Nick Smith]] has also called on the Government to lift the blanket ban on foreign ships, citing the case of the [[American Samoa]]–registered tuna fishing vessel ''Captain Vincent Gann'', which was denied entry by [[Immigration New Zealand]] and asked to seek urgent repairs in [[Hawaii]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Vessels barred from repairs in New Zealand costing jobs, Aimex warns |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/418077/vessels-barred-from-repairs-in-new-zealand-costing-jobs-aimex-warns |accessdate=2 June 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=2 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602224721/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/418077/vessels-barred-from-repairs-in-new-zealand-costing-jobs-aimex-warns |archivedate=2 June 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Sivignon |first1=Cherie |title=Covid-19 ship ban puts Nelson marine engineering jobs at risk |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121693148/covid19-ship-ban-puts-nelson-marine-engineering-jobs-at-risk |accessdate=2 June 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=2 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602224941/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121693148/covid19-ship-ban-puts-nelson-marine-engineering-jobs-at-risk |archivedate=2 June 2020}}</ref>

====Media====
On 30 March 2020 [[NZME]], which owns ''[[The New Zealand Herald]]'' and radio station [[Newstalk ZB]], announced the closure of [[Radio Sport]] with immediate effect, due to the [[Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on sports|impact of the coronavirus on sport]].<ref>{{cite news |title=The New Zealand Herald owner confirms closure of Radio Sport |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120669523/nz-herald-owner-understood-to-be-discussing-job-losses |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200331220644/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120669523/nz-herald-owner-understood-to-be-discussing-job-losses |access-date=14 April 2020 |archive-date=31 March 2020 |date=30 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]]}}</ref>

On 1 April, [[MediaWorks New Zealand|Mediaworks]]' Chief Executive Michael Anderson told staff to take a 15% wage cut in order to avoid redundancies.<ref>{{cite news |title=Mediaworks staff asked to take 15 percent pay cut |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413142/mediaworks-staff-asked-to-take-15-percent-pay-cut |accessdate=23 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=1 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403060354/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413142/mediaworks-staff-asked-to-take-15-percent-pay-cut |archivedate=3 April 2020}}</ref>

On 14 April, NZME announced that they were laying off 15% of their workforce (roughly 200 jobs) as a result of the economic fallout caused by the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Edmunds |first1=Susan |last2=Pullar-Strecker |first2=Tom |title=Media company NZME cuts workforce by 15% |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120995004/media-company-nzme-will-cut-its-workforce-by-15 |accessdate=13 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=14 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200413222719/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120995004/media-company-nzme-will-cut-its-workforce-by-15 |archivedate=13 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Live Covid-19 updates from New Zealand and around the world on 14 April |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414159/live-covid-19-updates-from-new-zealand-and-around-the-world-on-14-april |accessdate=13 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=14 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200413223203/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414159/live-covid-19-updates-from-new-zealand-and-around-the-world-on-14-april |archivedate=13 April 2020}}</ref>

On 16 April, [[Stuff (company)|Stuff]] Chief Executive [[Sinead Boucher]] asked staff earning more than $50,000 to take a 15% pay cut while the executive team will take a 25% pay cut. Boucher herself will take a 40% pay cut.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19: Stuff employees asked to take a 15 percent pay cut |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/414387/covid-19-stuff-employees-asked-to-take-a-15-percent-pay-cut |accessdate=23 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=16 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200423033144/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/414387/covid-19-stuff-employees-asked-to-take-a-15-percent-pay-cut |archivedate=23 April 2020}}</ref>

On 25 May, MediaWorks' CEO Michael Anderson announced that the company would be eliminating 130 jobs in its sales, out-of-home, and radio divisions as a result of the economic effects of the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |title=MediaWorks announces 130 job losses |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/417449/mediaworks-announces-130-job-losses |accessdate=25 May 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=25 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200525051248/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/417449/mediaworks-announces-130-job-losses|archive-date=25 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Edmunds |first1=Susan |last2=Pullar-Strecker |first2=Tom |title=MediaWorks planning to cut 130 roles in restructure |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121613713/mediaworks-planning-to-cut-130-roles-in-restructure |accessdate=25 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=25 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200525051415/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121613713/mediaworks-planning-to-cut-130-roles-in-restructure|archive-date=25 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Dreive |first1=Duncan |title=Stuff bought by its CEO, MediaWorks announces mass layoffs in historic day for NZ media |url=https://thespinoff.co.nz/business/25-05-2020/stuff-bought-by-its-ceo-mediaworks-announces-mass-layoffs-in-historic-day-for-nz-media/ |accessdate=25 May 2020 |work=[[The Spinoff]] |date=25 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200525051514/https://thespinoff.co.nz/business/25-05-2020/stuff-bought-by-its-ceo-mediaworks-announces-mass-layoffs-in-historic-day-for-nz-media/|archive-date=25 May 2020}}</ref>

On 12 June, it was reported that national broadcaster [[TVNZ]] was planning to cut 100 jobs over the next few weeks in order to save $10 million and that the company was looking for a new head of news to replace [[John Gillespie (broadcaster)|John Gillespie]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Dillane |first1=Tom |title=TVNZ set to cut 100 jobs to find $10m while they recruit new head of news |url= https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12339483 |accessdate=12 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=12 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200612110711/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12339483 |archivedate=12 June 2020}}</ref>

====Rest homes====
On 12 August 2020, Aged Care Association chief executive Simon Wallace announced that all rest homes in New Zealand would go into full lockdown immediately until midnight Friday (14 August) in response to a recent wave of community transmissions.<ref>{{cite news |title=All rest homes going into level 4 lockdown for three days |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/423330/all-rest-homes-going-into-level-4-lockdown-for-three-days |accessdate=12 August 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=12 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200812032333/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/423330/all-rest-homes-going-into-level-4-lockdown-for-three-days |archivedate=12 August 2020}}</ref>

====Retail sector====
On 25 March 2020, [[The Warehouse Group]] prematurely announced that they were an "essential service" without consulting with the Government. When they were deemed not to be an essential service, the Warehouse shut down its brands including The Warehouse, Warehouse Stationery, Torpedo7, [[Noel Leeming]], 1-day and TheMarket for the duration of the four-week lockdown, with all staff being put on full paid leave. The company also faces a fine of $500,000 if it is found to have breached the [[New Zealand Exchange]]'s disclosure rules with more penalties if the company is found to have profited from a rise in its share price resulting from the announcement.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Edmunds |first1=Susan |last2=Foxcroft |first2=Debrin |title=The Warehouse share price 'likely to fall' |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120543993/more-clarity-on-whats-essential-whats-next-for-the-warehouse-shares |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=25 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327232419/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120543993/more-clarity-on-whats-essential-whats-next-for-the-warehouse-shares |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Kirkness |first1=Luke |title=Covid-19 coronavirus: The Warehouse, Torpedo 7, Noel Leeming, Warehouse Stationery staff to be paid in full during lockdown |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12319906 |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=25 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326194134/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12319906 |archive-date=26 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Should The Warehouse be liable for misleading stock market? |url=https://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/on-air/early-edition/audio/dean-anderson-should-the-warehouse-be-liable-for-misleading-stock-market/ |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=[[Newstalk ZB]] |date=27 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327203505/https://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/on-air/early-edition/audio/dean-anderson-should-the-warehouse-be-liable-for-misleading-stock-market/ |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 27 March, the national retail chain Mad Butcher was ordered to shut operations since it did not meet the Government's criteria of essential services. Mad-Butcher chief executive Michael Morton expressed frustration with a lack of clarity from the [[Ministry of Business, Innovation and Employment]] (MBIE). The company is projected to lose $3 million in meat.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Carroll |first1=Melanie |title=Mad Butcher stores closed after confusion, CEO gutted |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/120618325/mad-butcher-stores-closed-after-confusion-ceo-gutted |accessdate=27 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=27 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200327012106/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/120618325/mad-butcher-stores-closed-after-confusion-ceo-gutted |archive-date=27 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 10 April, hardware giant [[Mitre 10]] announced that it would lay off staff at its [[Albany, New Zealand|Albany]] support centre in Auckland. While the company's Mitre 10 and Mitre 10 Mega stores are closed, customers can still order trade supplies for essential services online and by phone for contactless collection and home delivery.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bayer |first1=Kurt |title=Covid-19: Mitre 10 confirms job losses |url=https://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/news/business/covid-19-mitre-10-confirms-job-losses/ |accessdate=10 April 2020 |work=[[Newstalk ZB]] |date=10 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200410042153/https://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/news/business/covid-19-mitre-10-confirms-job-losses/ |archivedate=10 April 2020}}</ref>

On 12 May, hardware and DIY chain [[Bunnings]] announced that it will close seven stores in [[Ashburton, New Zealand|Ashburton]], [[Hornby, New Zealand|Hornby]], [[Hastings, New Zealand|Hastings]], [[Cambridge, New Zealand|Cambridge]], [[Rangiora]], [[Te Awamutu]], and [[Putāruru|Putaruru]] with the loss of 145 jobs.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Gibson |first1=Anne |title=Bunnings to shut seven NZ stores, 145 staff affected |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12331340 |accessdate=12 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=12 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512090836/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12331340|archive-date=12 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Bunnings to close seven NZ stores, with 145 job cuts |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/416450/bunnings-to-close-seven-nz-stores-with-145-job-cuts |accessdate=12 May 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=12 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200512092649/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/416450/bunnings-to-close-seven-nz-stores-with-145-job-cuts |archivedate=12 May 2020}}</ref>

On 25 May, it was reported that the department store chain [[H & J Smith]] was considering closing its stores in [[Dunedin]], [[Mosgiel]], [[Balclutha, New Zealand|Balclutha]], [[Te Anau]], and [[Gore, New Zealand|Gore]] as well as the Armoury Store in Dunedin and Outdoor World in [[Queenstown, New Zealand|Queenstown]]. The Take Note store in Gore would relocate but H & J Smith's stores in [[Invercargill]] and Queenstown would remain open. A final decision will be made in early June.<ref>{{cite news |title=H&J Smith looking to close South Island stores |url= https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12334703 |accessdate=26 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=25 May 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200526085811/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12334703 |archivedate=26 May 2020}}</ref><ref name="ODT H&J Smith">{{cite news |last1=Miller |first1=Grant |title=Mayor urges retailer to reconsider closure plans |url= https://www.odt.co.nz/news/dunedin/mayor-urges-retailer-reconsider-closure-plans |accessdate=26 May 2020 |work=[[Otago Daily Times]] |date=26 May 2020|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200526090510/https://www.odt.co.nz/news/dunedin/mayor-urges-retailer-reconsider-closure-plans|archive-date=26 May 2020}}</ref><ref name="Stuff H&J Smith">{{cite news |last1=Rowe |first1=Damian |title=Dunedin mayor urges H&J Smith to remain open in city |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121629539/dunedin-mayor-urges-hj-smith-to-remain-open-in-city |accessdate=26 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=26 May 2020|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200526090642/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121629539/dunedin-mayor-urges-hj-smith-to-remain-open-in-city|archive-date=26 May 2020}}</ref> Dunedin and Clutha Mayors [[Aaron Hawkins (politician)|Aaron Hawkins]] and [[Bryan Cadogan]] have urged the company to reconsider their closure plans.<ref name="ODT H&J Smith" /><ref name="Stuff H&J Smith" />

On 20 July, the Warehouse CEO Pejman Okhovat announced that it could cut between 500 and 750 jobs as part of a proposed restructuring of the company. First Union general secretary Dennis Maga has criticised the company for using COVID-19 as an excuse to lay off hundreds of workers and to reduce the incomes of thousands of workers.<ref>{{cite news |title=The Warehouse could cut up to 750 jobs, company says |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/421564/the-warehouse-could-cut-up-to-750-jobs-company-says |accessdate=20 July 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=20 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200720000256/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/421564/the-warehouse-could-cut-up-to-750-jobs-company-says|archive-date=20 July 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Foxcroft |first1=Debrin |last2=Edmunds |first2=Susan |title=950 jobs to go: Union says The Warehouse using Covid-19 excuse |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300060721/950-jobs-to-go-union-says-the-warehouse-using-covid19-excuse |accessdate=20 July 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=20 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200720000424/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300060721/950-jobs-to-go-union-says-the-warehouse-using-covid19-excuse |archivedate=20 July 2020}}</ref>

On 19 August, the supermarket chain [[Countdown (supermarket)|Countdown]] temporarily closed two of its Auckland stores for cleaning after health authorities confirmed that they had been visited by two individuals who had tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Two Countdown supermarkets in Auckland close after customers test positive for Covid |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12357928 |accessdate=19 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=19 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200819064409/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12357928 |archivedate=19 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> On 22 August, Countdown shut down two more of its supermarkets in Auckland for cleaning after health authorities confirmed that an infected individual had visited those stores.<ref>{{cite news |title=Two Auckland Countdown stores close for cleaning after shopper tests positive for Covid-19 |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/two-auckland-countdown-stores-close-cleaning-after-shopper-tests-positive-covid-19 |accessdate=22 August 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=22 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200822081347/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/two-auckland-countdown-stores-close-cleaning-after-shopper-tests-positive-covid-19 |archivedate=22 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 26 August 2020, stationery supply company [[OfficeMax]] announced that it would be closing all 14 of its New Zealand branches and shift operations online in response to growing online usage and the economic effects of the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Shaw |first1=Aimee |title=OfficeMax set to shut down its retail stores |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/business/news/article.cfm?c_id=3&objectid=12359718 |accessdate=26 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=26 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Foxcroft |first1=Debrin |title=OfficeMax closing its shops in New Zealand |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/industries/122568682/officemax-closing-its-shops-in-new-zealand |accessdate=26 August 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=26 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 8 September 2020, supermarket chain Countdown closed its [[New Lynn]] supermarket temporarily for a "deep clean" after an individual who tested positive for COVID-19 visited the store the previous Friday.<ref>{{cite news |title=West Auckland supermarket closes after visit from Covid-positive person |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/west-auckland-supermarket-closes-after-visit-covid-positive-person |accessdate=8 September 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=8 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200908090135/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/west-auckland-supermarket-closes-after-visit-covid-positive-person |archivedate=8 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Sports and recreation====
On 22 October, the [[North Shore, New Zealand|North Shore]] gym "Snap Fitness" closed for five days after a person who later tested positive for COVID-19 visited the premises.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Moodie |first1=Kim |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Positive case visited Auckland marine supply store, no one considered close contacts |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-positive-case-visited-auckland-marine-supply-store-no-one-considered-close-contacts/P52FF5BJBCBYTT5S4NPA2434TY/ |accessdate=22 October 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=22 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201022092200/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-positive-case-visited-auckland-marine-supply-store-no-one-considered-close-contacts/P52FF5BJBCBYTT5S4NPA2434TY/ |archivedate=22 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Telecommunications providers====
On 14 April, telco [[2degrees]] announced that they were to cut the workforce by 10% (i.e. 120 staff), stop recruitment, and reduce spending on capital projects.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pullar-Strecker |first1=Tom |title=2degrees proposes to cut its workforce by 10% |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121012411/2degrees-proposes-to-cut-its-workforce-by-10 |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=14 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415114153/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121012411/2degrees-proposes-to-cut-its-workforce-by-10|archive-date=15 April 2020}}</ref>

On 10 September, [[pay television]] company [[Sky (New Zealand)|Sky]] reported a loss of NZ$175 million, down 74% the previous year, after it wrote-down the value of its assets by $178m to reflect the economic uncertainty caused by the COVID-19 pandemic. While commercial and advertising revenue was affected by the pandemic, revenue from streaming was up by 35 percent, contributing to an overall revenue figure of NZ$747.6 million.<ref>{{cite news |title=Sky posts loss after business writedown |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/425688/sky-posts-loss-after-business-writedown |accessdate=10 September 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=10 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200910053012/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/business/425688/sky-posts-loss-after-business-writedown |archivedate=10 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> The company had also laid off 200 workers (roughly 18%) of its workforce since June 2019.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pullar-Strecker |first1=Tom |title=Return of international sports and set-top box upgrade light at end of tunnel for Sky TV |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122681735/return-of-international-sports-and-settop-box-upgrade-light-at-end-of-tunnel-for-sky-tv |accessdate=10 September 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=10 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200910053622/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122681735/return-of-international-sports-and-settop-box-upgrade-light-at-end-of-tunnel-for-sky-tv |archivedate=10 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Tourism sector====
The imposition of border restrictions has had a major effect on the international tourism sector. For the month of February 2020, the number of international visitors arriving in New Zealand fell 11% compared to February 2019, mostly driven by a 90% drop in visitors from mainland China.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Border restrictions impact visitor arrivals {{!}} Stats NZ|url=https://www.stats.govt.nz/news/border-restrictions-impact-visitor-arrivals|website=www.stats.govt.nz|access-date=14 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200421125034/https://www.stats.govt.nz/news/border-restrictions-impact-visitor-arrivals|archive-date=21 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> In March 2020, international visitor arrivals fell 54% compared to March 2019.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Border restrictions cause major drop in visitor arrivals {{!}} Stats NZ|url=https://www.stats.govt.nz/news/border-restrictions-cause-major-drop-in-visitor-arrivals|website=www.stats.govt.nz|access-date=14 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200514001957/https://www.stats.govt.nz/news/border-restrictions-cause-major-drop-in-visitor-arrivals|archive-date=14 May 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 8 April 2020 travel company [[Flight Centre]] announced that it would close 58 stores permanently. Flight Centre also announced that it was laying off 300 employees temporarily and 250 employees permanently.<ref>{{cite news |title=Flight Centre shuts 58 stores indefinitely, stands down more than 300 employees during Covid-19 crisis |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/flight-centre-shuts-58-stores-indefinitely-stands-down-more-than-300-employees-during-covid-19-crisis |accessdate=10 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=8 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200410035936/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/flight-centre-shuts-58-stores-indefinitely-stands-down-more-than-300-employees-during-covid-19-crisis|archive-date=10 April 2020}}</ref><ref>
{{cite news |last1= Sadler |first1=Rachel |title=Coronavirus: Flight Centre closing 58 New Zealand stores |url= https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/travel/2020/04/coronavirus-flight-centre-closing-58-new-zealand-stores.html |accessdate=10 April 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=8 April 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200410040055/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/travel/2020/04/coronavirus-flight-centre-closing-58-new-zealand-stores.html |archivedate=10 April 2020}}</ref>

In early May, ''[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]]'' reported that thousands of migrant workers have been left unemployed in the tourist town of [[Queenstown, New Zealand|Queenstown]] with no money for food or rent. According to [[Queenstown-Lakes District]] mayor [[Jim Boult]], 6,000 migrants had requested welfare assistance from local authorities.<ref>{{cite news |last1= McKenzie-McLean |first1= Jo |title= Coronavirus: Unfair for Kiwis to turn backs on migrant workers |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121395546/coronavirus-unfair-for-kiwis-to-turn-backs-on-migrant-workers |accessdate= 6 May 2020 |work= [[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date= 5 May 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200513022558/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/121395546/coronavirus-unfair-for-kiwis-to-turn-backs-on-migrant-workers |archive-date= 13 May 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref>

on 25 June, it was reported that [[bungy jumping]] company [[AJ Hackett Bungy]] had been able to save 20 jobs as a result of a $10.2 million bail-out package from the government. This package also allows the company to reopen 13 of its branches in Queenstown, Auckland, and Taupo.<ref>{{cite news |last1=McKew |first1=Matthew |title=Staff speechless over bungy bail-out |url=https://www.odt.co.nz/regions/queenstown/staff-speechless-over-bungy-bail-out |accessdate=24 June 2020 |work=[[Otago Daily Times]] |date=25 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200624234918/https://www.odt.co.nz/regions/queenstown/staff-speechless-over-bungy-bail-out |archivedate=24 June 2020}}</ref>

===Civil society responses===
[[File:Covid-19 empty bread shelves.jpg|alt=Empty bread shelves at a supermarket in Wellington after panic buying|thumb|Empty bread shelves at a supermarket in Wellington after panic buying (22 March 2020)]]
Increased demand for face masks and hand sanitisers led to shortages nationwide in supermarkets and pharmacies.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Clent|first1=Danielle|url= pharmacies|work=Stuff|date=1 March 2020|access-date=5 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12309400|title=Wellington supermarket limits hand sanitiser sales to two items per customer|work =The New Zealand Herald|date=18 February 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200304205515/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12309400|archive-date=4 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Following the first New Zealand case of COVID-19 on 28 February, customers were reportedly panic-buying supplies at Auckland supermarkets.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Deguara|first1=Brittney|url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/410699/coronavirus-retailers-confident-of-supply-chain-despite-panic-buying|title=Coronavirus: Retailers confident of supply chain despite 'panic' buying|website=RNZ|date=1 March 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200302132501/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/410699/coronavirus-retailers-confident-of-supply-chain-despite-panic-buying|archive-date=2 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last1=Deguara|first1=Brittney|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/auckland/local-news/119915529/coronavirus-stock-piling-customer-demand-forces-auckland-supermarket-to-close-its-doors|title=Coronavirus stockpiling: Customer demand forces Auckland wholesaler to close its doors|work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]]|date=29 February 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200303193249/https://www.stuff.co.nz/auckland/local-news/119915529/coronavirus-stock-piling-customer-demand-forces-auckland-supermarket-to-close-its-doors|archive-date=3 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

Following the implementation of stronger border controls, [[SANZAAR]] announced on 14 March that it would suspend play of its [[Super Rugby]] season (which features five New Zealand teams) following the conclusion of that weekend's matches.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.smh.com.au/sport/rugby-union/all-super-rugby-matches-to-be-cancelled-after-sunday-s-fixtures-20200314-p54a4u.html|title=All Super Rugby matches to be cancelled after Sunday's fixtures|last=Decent|first=Tom|date=14 March 2020|work=[[Sydney Morning Herald]]|language=en|access-date=14 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200315184711/https://www.smh.com.au/sport/rugby-union/all-super-rugby-matches-to-be-cancelled-after-sunday-s-fixtures-20200314-p54a4u.html|archive-date=15 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 15 March, it was announced that the [[Warbirds Over Wanaka]] 2020 airshow was cancelled due to the Government's response to the pandemic.<ref>{{Cite web|url= https://www.warbirdsoverwanaka.com/2020-airshow/covid19/|title=Warbirds Over Wanaka International Airshow – Cancelled 15.3.20|date=15 March 2020|website=Warbirds Over Wanaka|language=en-NZ|access-date=17 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403091812/https://www.warbirdsoverwanaka.com/2020-airshow/covid19/|archive-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> This was the first time in the biennial event's history that it had been cancelled.{{citation needed|date=April 2020}}

On 19 March, the [[Royal New Zealand Returned and Services' Association]] announced that all Anzac Day services, scheduled for 25 April, would be cancelled and the red poppy collection postponed due to the health risk. This was the first time that Anzac Day services have not been held since 1916.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wiltshire |first1=Laura |title=Anzac Day services cancelled due to coronavirus |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120399099/anzac-day-services-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus |accessdate=19 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=19 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200318221258/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120399099/anzac-day-services-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus |archive-date=18 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

====Māori responses====
A Wellington [[iwi]] placed a ''taupāruru'' (restriction) on the practice of [[hongi]], a traditional [[Māori people|Māori]] greeting, in response to the outbreak.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/te-manu-korihi/410992/coronavirus-hongi-restriction-put-in-place-at-pohiri-in-wellington|title=Coronavirus: Hongi restriction put in place at pōhiri in Wellington|work=[[Radio New Zealand]]|date=5 March 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305052427/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/te-manu-korihi/410992/coronavirus-hongi-restriction-put-in-place-at-pohiri-in-wellington|archive-date=5 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 24 March, former [[Tai Tokerau]] Member of Parliament [[Hone Harawira]] announced that local iwi in the [[Far North District|Far North]] were working with local authorities and [[Mayor of Far North]] [[John Carter (New Zealand politician)|John Carter]] to set up roadblocks to prevent foreign tourists from travelling into the area. Tourists in the area would be encouraged to leave the Far North. Roadblocks were set up at State Highway 1 at [[Whakapara]] and State Highway 12 at [[Waipoua]]. Harawira criticised the Government for not stopping tourists from entering the country prior to the border closure.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Williams |first1=Caroline |last2=Biddle |first2=Donna-Lee |title=Coronavirus: Iwi across NZ step up tourist blockades, close huts and walkways |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120511786/coronavirus-hone-harawira-to-blockade-tourists-from-far-north?rm=m |accessdate=26 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=24 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200401052018/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120511786/coronavirus-hone-harawira-to-blockade-tourists-from-far-north?rm=m |archive-date=1 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> By 26 March, at least three groups of tourists had been stopped from entering the Far North. A testing centre was also set up at Waiomio Hill to test locals returning from overseas.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Biddle |first1=Donna-Lee |title=Coronavirus: Tourists turned away at Far North checkpoints |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120569981/coronavirus-tourists-turned-away-at-far-north-checkpoints |accessdate=26 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=26 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200325225039/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120569981/coronavirus-tourists-turned-away-at-far-north-checkpoints |archive-date=25 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Having set up illegal road blocks to stop people from bringing the virus into the Far North, Hone Harawira broke Level 4 Lockdown restrictions to make a 600&nbsp;km round trip to Auckland, then a virus hot spot, on 12 April. Harawira claimed that the purpose of the trip was to obtain medical supplies and visiting his sister was unimportant.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Piper |first1=Denise |title=Coronavirus: Hone Harawira says 600km trip, meal with family in Auckland 'was safe' |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120998428/coronavirus-hone-harawira-says-600km-trip-meal-with-family-in-auckland-was-safe |accessdate=18 August 2020 |issue=national/health/coronavirus |publisher=Stuff Limited |date=14 April 2020}}</ref>

Similar measures were put in place on the East Cape area of the North Island.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Graham-McLay |first1=Charlotte |title=New Zealand's Māori tribes set up checkpoints to avoid 'catastrophic' coronavirus deaths |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/24/new-zealands-maori-tribes-set-up-checkpoints-to-avoid-catastrophic-coronavirus-deaths |accessdate=31 March 2020 |work=[[The Guardian]]|date=23 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200427221819/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/mar/24/new-zealands-maori-tribes-set-up-checkpoints-to-avoid-catastrophic-coronavirus-deaths|archive-date=27 April 2020}}</ref> In April, there were reports that iwi checkpoints in the central North Island, East Coast, and Northland were obstructing essential travel by local residents. National Member of Parliament for Northland [[Matt King (politician)|Matt King]] said that constituents had complained about being verbally abused and spat upon at iwi checkpoints in Northland.<ref name="Stuff 21 April 2020">{{cite news |last1=Walton |first1=Steven |title=Coronavirus: Illegal checkpoints being dealt with, but ones with support OK – minister |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121153028/coronavirus-illegal-checkpoints-being-dealt-with-but-ones-with-support-ok--minister |accessdate=6 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=21 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200428080849/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121153028/coronavirus-illegal-checkpoints-being-dealt-with-but-ones-with-support-ok--minister |archivedate=28 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="1 News iwi checkpoints">{{cite news |last1=Castles |first1=Helen |title=Some iwi-led checkpoints causing tension as they continue through Alert Level 3 |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/some-iwi-led-checkpoints-causing-tension-they-continue-through-alert-level-3 |accessdate=6 May 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=30 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200506095530/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/some-iwi-led-checkpoints-causing-tension-they-continue-through-alert-level-3 |archivedate=6 May 2020}}</ref> In response, [[Minister of Police (New Zealand)|Police Minister]] [[Stuart Nash]] warned that the Police would take action against "illegal" checkpoints that had been set up without police support while allowing checkpoints in remote towns as long as they had the support of the local police and community.<ref name="Stuff 21 April 2020"/>

In early May 2020, [[Newshub]] reported that the iwi [[Te Whānau-ā-Apanui]] in the eastern Bay of Plenty region had been operating an unauthorised travel permit system to protect the region's elderly population, horticulture, and agricultural industries. This included a requirement for essential workers to provide a letter from the [[Ministry for Primary Industries (New Zealand)|Ministry for Primary Industries]] proving that their travel complied with lockdown rules, which were eased when Alert Level 4 came to an end on 28 April. On 6 May, the New Zealand Police clarified that community road block operators in the Bay of Plenty did not have the authority to turn away New Zealanders lacking the necessary travel documents.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Burrows |first1=Matt |title=Coronavirus: Community roadblocks turn Bay of Plenty locals away for not having 'travel permit' from local iwi Te Whānau-ā-Apanui |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-community-roadblocks-turn-bay-of-plenty-locals-away-for-not-having-travel-permit-from-local-iwi-te-wh-nau-apanui.html |accessdate=6 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=5 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200506111907/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-community-roadblocks-turn-bay-of-plenty-locals-away-for-not-having-travel-permit-from-local-iwi-te-wh-nau-apanui.html |archivedate=6 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Burrows |first1=Mtt |title=Coronavirus: Local iwi's 'travel permits' at Bay of Plenty community roadblocks mean nothing, police say |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-local-iwi-s-travel-permits-at-bay-of-plenty-community-roadblocks-mean-nothing-police-say.html |accessdate=6 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=6 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200506112348/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-local-iwi-s-travel-permits-at-bay-of-plenty-community-roadblocks-mean-nothing-police-say.html |archivedate=6 May 2020}}</ref>

====Faith communities' responses====
In mid-March, several faith communities and denominations including the [[Catholic Church in New Zealand|Catholic Church]], the Supreme Sikh Society, the [[The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in New Zealand|Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints]], and LIFE church announced that they would be cancelling or reducing large gatherings and taking more health precautions in response to the Government's ban on gatherings with more than 100 people. However, Bishop [[Brian Tamaki]]'s [[Destiny Church (New Zealand)|Destiny Church]] initially refused to close their services, with Tamaki stating that they would not let a "filthy virus" scare them out of attending church.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Stewart |first1=Indira |title=NZ churches back govt restrictions, cancel mass gatherings. Except Destiny |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/national/programmes/first-up/audio/2018738815/nz-churches-back-govt-restrictions-cancel-mass-gatherings-except-destiny |accessdate=28 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=17 March 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328035551/https://www.rnz.co.nz/national/programmes/first-up/audio/2018738815/nz-churches-back-govt-restrictions-cancel-mass-gatherings-except-destiny |archivedate=28 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> In response, infectious diseases expert Dr [[Siouxsie Wiles]] criticised Bishop Tamaki for undermining efforts to keep New Zealanders safe.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Harvey |first1=Megan |title=Coronavirus: Experts slams Brian Tamaki's attitude as he vows to keep churches open |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12316991 |accessdate=28 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=16 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200328070208/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12316991 |archive-date=28 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

Smaller congregations like Elim Church and C3 Church in [[Marlborough Region|Marlborough]] have halved services in order to comply with the Government's ban on gatherings with more than 100 people while the Nativity Church has set up networks to support parishioners.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Angeloni |first1=Alice |title=Coronavirus: Church plans multiple Sunday services, others 'likely' to cancel after gathering ban |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120419551/coronavirus-church-plans-multiple-sunday-services-others-likely-to-cancel-after-gathering-ban |accessdate=28 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=19 March 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200319190838/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120419551/coronavirus-church-plans-multiple-sunday-services-others-likely-to-cancel-after-gathering-ban |archive-date=19 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 20 March, the [[New Zealand Catholic Bishops' Conference]] declared that all public [[Mass in the Catholic Church|Masses]] would be suspended for the foreseeable future. This decision was made in line with the government's decision to cancel mass indoor events with more than 100 people.<ref>{{Cite web|url= https://chchcatholic.nz/2020/03/bishops-conference-pastoral-letter-regarding-covid-19/|title=Bishops Conference Pastoral Letter regarding Covid-19|date=20 March 2020|website=Catholic Diocese of Christchurch|language=en-US|access-date=23 March 2020|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200323003921/https://chchcatholic.nz/2020/03/bishops-conference-pastoral-letter-regarding-covid-19/|archive-date=23 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 29 March, it was reported that members of the exclusive [[Gloriavale Christian Community]] were not complying with lockdown measures and that daycare centres, schools, and meetings were still ongoing. The Police have since announced that they are working with Gloriavale to make sure that its members abided with lockdown restrictions.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Gloriavale breaking lockdown rules – Support Trust |url= https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412843/coronavirus-gloriavale-breaking-lockdown-rules-support-trust |accessdate=29 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=29 March 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200329004516/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412843/coronavirus-gloriavale-breaking-lockdown-rules-support-trust |archivedate=29 March 2020}}</ref>

In late March 2020, there were reports that members of the [[Islam in New Zealand|Muslim community]] in New Zealand were having trouble accessing [[halal]] food due to the closure of butcheries, which were not deemed an "essential service" under Alert Level 4.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Hall |first1=Kristin |title=Concern among Muslims that halal butcher closures will see them miss out in lockdown |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/concern-among-muslims-halal-butcher-closures-see-them-miss-in-lockdown |accessdate=14 May 2020 |date=28 March 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200409120630/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/concern-among-muslims-halal-butcher-closures-see-them-miss-in-lockdown |archivedate=9 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Andelane |first1=Lana |title=Jacinda Ardern 'aware of' issues for people accessing halal meat |url= https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/jacinda-ardern-aware-of-issues-for-people-accessing-halal-meat.html |accessdate=14 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=29 March 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200411041840/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/jacinda-ardern-aware-of-issues-for-people-accessing-halal-meat.html |archivedate=11 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Keogh |first1=Brittany |title=Coronavirus: Community safety trumps access to halal meat, Muslim man says |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120701883/coronavirus-community-safety-trumps-access-to-halal-meat-muslim-man-says |accessdate=14 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=31 March 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200415000508/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120701883/coronavirus-community-safety-trumps-access-to-halal-meat-muslim-man-says |archivedate=15 April 2020}}</ref>

Under the Government's Alert Level 2 restrictions which came into force on 14 May, religious gatherings have been limited to ten persons despite the Government stating that they could have a 100-person limit. The [[Federation of Islamic Associations of New Zealand]] (FIANZ) issued a press release that New Zealand Muslims would be unable to hold their [[Muslim holidays|Eid]] prayers at mosques and community centers due to the ten person limit on private gatherings.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Mohammad |first1=Rizwan |title=FIANZ circular confirms Eid prayers will not be held in New Zealand this year|url= https://www.indianweekender.co.nz/Pages/ArticleDetails/7/12320/New-Zealand/FIANZ-circular-confirms-Eid-prayer-will-not-be-held-in-New-Zealand-this-year |accessdate=22 May 2020 |work=The Indian Weekender |date=12 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200520000320/https://www.indianweekender.co.nz/Pages/ArticleDetails/7/12320/New-Zealand/FIANZ-circular-confirms-Eid-prayer-will-not-be-held-in-New-Zealand-this-year |archivedate=20 May 2020}}</ref>  The Catholic bishops of New Zealand have expressed disappointment with the ten-person limit, describing the measures as too restrictive.<ref>{{cite web |title=Covid-19: Churches in New Zealand to re-open without religious services |url= https://www.vaticannews.va/en/church/news/2020-05/covid-19-churches-in-zealand-to-re-open-without-religious-servi.html |publisher=[[Vatican News]] |accessdate=14 May 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200514031412/https://www.vaticannews.va/en/church/news/2020-05/covid-19-churches-in-zealand-to-re-open-without-religious-servi.html |archivedate=14 May 2020 |date=12 May 2020}}</ref> Meanwhile, Bishop Tamaki of Destiny Church has announced that his movement would be holding services in defiance of Level 2 lockdown restrictions.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bhatia |first1=Ripu |title=Coronavirus: Destiny Church leader Brian Tamaki says Sunday service will go ahead |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300010278/coronavirus-destiny-church-leader-brian-tamaki-says-sunday-service-will-go-ahead |accessdate=14 May 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=12 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200514025725/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300010278/coronavirus-destiny-church-leader-brian-tamaki-says-sunday-service-will-go-ahead |archivedate=14 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Brian Tamaki to hold church service this weekend despite Level 2 restrictions |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/brian-tamaki-hold-church-service-weekend-despite-level-2-restrictions |accessdate=14 May 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=13 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200514030133/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/brian-tamaki-hold-church-service-weekend-despite-level-2-restrictions |archivedate=14 May 2020}}</ref> The New Zealand Muslim Association President Ikhlaq Kashkari has expressed disappointment that the ten person limit will prevent mosques from gathering for [[Ramadan]]. The Minister of Commoners Weslyan Methodist Community Reverend Frank Ritchie has also criticised the perceived double standard towards faith communities.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wilkins |first1=Alice |title=Coronavirus: Religious leaders, communities 'distraught' over alert level 2 rules banning congregations |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-religious-leaders-communities-distraught-over-alert-level-2-rules-banning-congregations.html |accessdate=14 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=13 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200514105918/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-religious-leaders-communities-distraught-over-alert-level-2-rules-banning-congregations.html |archivedate=14 May 2020}}</ref>

On 25 May, the Government raised the limit on religious services from ten to 100 persons, allowing many faith communities to resume mass gatherings.<ref name="NewstalkZB 25 May" /><ref name="RNZ 25 May" /><ref name="Stuff 25 May" />

On 29 August, [[1 News]] reported that several members of [[Mount Roskill]] Evangelical Fellowship Church had continued to meet privately despite the Level 3 lockdown that had come into force in the [[Auckland Region]] between 12 and 30 August.<ref>{{cite news |title=Members from Mt Roskill church gathered for prayer meetings during lockdown |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/members-mt-roskill-church-gathered-prayer-meetings-during-lockdown |accessdate=30 August 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=29 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200829123919/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/members-mt-roskill-church-gathered-prayer-meetings-during-lockdown |archivedate=29 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Health authorities had earlier identified the church as a sub-cluster of the Auckland August cluster.<ref name="Stuff Mt Roskill" /> On 31 August, Health Minister [[Chris Hipkins]] announced that health authorities were investigating claims that the church held meetings during Auckland's Alert Level 3 restrictions. Microbiologist Siouxsie Wiles also said that genome sequencing would be used to prove whether cases at the church were linked to the Auckland cluster. 15 COVID-19 cases have been linked to the Mt Roskill church sub-cluster.<ref name="Mt Roskill meetings 31 August 2020">{{cite news |last1=Tokalau |first1=Torika |title=Coronavirus: Church investigated over allegation meetings were held in lockdown |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/122617065/coronavirus-church-investigated-over-allegation-meetings-were-held-in-lockdown |accessdate=1 September 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=31 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200831233130/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/122617065/coronavirus-church-investigated-over-allegation-meetings-were-held-in-lockdown |archivedate=31 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 10 September, several Christian leaders including Pacific Response Coordination Team chairman Pakilau Manase Lua and [[Wesleyan Church|Wesleyan Methodist]] minister Frank Ritchie expressed concern about misinformation relating to COVID-19 circulating among New Zealand congregants attending churches with links to conservative [[Evangelicalism|evangelical]] and [[Pentecostalism|Pentecostal]] churches in the United States.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bradley |first1=Anusha |title=Churches with links to the US being blamed for spreading Covid-19 misinformation |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/425669/churches-with-links-to-the-us-being-blamed-for-spreading-covid-19-misinformation |accessdate=10 September 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=10 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200909184242/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/425669/churches-with-links-to-the-us-being-blamed-for-spreading-covid-19-misinformation |archivedate=10 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Mass gatherings and protests====
=====George Floyd protests=====
{{Main|George Floyd protests in New Zealand}}
On 1 June, [[Black Lives Matter]] (BLM) [[International George Floyd protests#Oceania|solidarity protests]] were held in several major centres including Auckland, Wellington, Christchurch, Dunedin, [[Tauranga]], [[Palmerston North]] and [[Hamilton, New Zealand|Hamilton]] in response to the [[killing of George Floyd]], which had sparked a wave of protests and riots in the United States and around the world. 4,000 people attended the Auckland rally alone, which saw participants marching from [[Aotea Square]] down [[Queen Street, Auckland|Queen Street]] to the American Consulate General. In Wellington, hundreds gathered outside Parliament. According to media reports, there was little social distancing due to the large volume of participants.<ref>{{cite news |title=New Zealand protests live: Protester ties himself to US Embassy in Wellington |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?objectid=12336288 |accessdate=1 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=1 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200601074459/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?objectid=12336288 |archivedate=1 June 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Block |first1=George |last2=Kenny |first2=Lee |last3=Flahive |first3=Brad |last4=Piper |first4=Denise |title=Black Lives Matter marches: Thousands of Kiwis peacefully protest against racism Microbiologist and health adviser Dr. [[Siouxsie Wiles]], Deputy Prime Minister [[Winston Peters]], and [[ACT New Zealand|ACT Party]] leader [[David Seymour (New Zealand politician)|David Seymour]] have criticized march participants for flouting Level 2 lockdown restrictions. Dr Wiles called for people who attended the BLM marches and gatherings to self-isolate for 14 days. Peters and Seymour criticised participants for violating Alert Level 2 lockdown restrictions and undermining efforts to eliminate COVID-19, while calling on the Government to move towards Alert Level 1.<ref>{{cite news |title=New Zealand protests live: Social distancing concerns as thousands attend protests |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12336288 |accessdate=1 June 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=1 June 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602112418/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12336288|archive-date=2 June 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Cheng Zealand Herald]] |date=1 June 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200602112741/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12336332|archive-date=2 June 2020}}</ref> Prime Minister Jacinda Ardern has criticised protesters for violating Level 2 restrictions in the midst of a global pandemic, while expressing sympathy for [[George Floyd]].<ref>{{cite news |title='We are |last1=Whyte |first1=Anna |title=Police Minister understands Black Lives Matter protestors will not be prosecuted
