2020}}</ref>

In response, Christchurch BLM protest organiser Will Hunter defended his decision to hold the rally, which attracted 700 people. He also said that he and his fellow organisers had urged participants to take health precautions including wearing gloves, masks, social distancing and staying at home if sick.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Theunissen |first1=Matthew |title=Christchurch Black Lives Matter protest organiser stands firm |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/418099/christchurch-black-lives-matter-protest-organiser-stands-firm |accessdate=4 June 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=4 June 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200604082846/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/418099/christchurch-black-lives-matter-protest-organiser-stands-firm |archivedate=4 June 2020}}</ref>

=====Anti-lockdown protests=====
{{Main|COVID-19 anti-lockdown protests in New Zealand}}
  
On 13 August 2020, 60 protesters from two groups, FACTS NZ and the Kotahitanga Movement Aotearoa, held a protest march against the Government's COVID-19 lockdown in [[Whangārei]]. The participants included [[New Zealand Public Party]] leader [[Billy Te Kahika]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pearse |first1=Adam |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Lockdown protest stops traffic in Whangārei |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?objectid=12356284&ref=recommended |accessdate=16 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=13 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200816075531/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?objectid=12356284&ref=recommended |archivedate=16 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 22 August, 100 anti-lockdown protesters peacefully demonstrated in Auckland's Queen Street. The protest was organised by the NZ Liberty March with several not wearing masks, criticising the Government's lockdown policy and making "health claims" about COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news |title=Anti-lockdown protestors gather in Auckland's Aotea Square before march down Queen St |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/anti-lockdown-protestors-gather-in-aucklands-aotea-square-before-march-down-queen-st |accessdate=22 August 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=22 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200822075234/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/anti-lockdown-protestors-gather-in-aucklands-aotea-square-before-march-down-queen-st |archivedate=22 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: 'We will not be silenced' - Maskless anti-lockdown protestors march in Auckland |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12358696 |accessdate=22 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=22 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200822080934/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12358696 |archivedate=22 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 29 August, hundreds of anti-lockdown protesters gathered in Auckland's Queen Street. This "liberty march" was attended by [[Advance New Zealand]] party co-leader [[Jami-Lee Ross]] and [[New Conservative Party (New Zealand)|New Conservative Party]] deputy leader [[Elliot Ikilei]]. Several attendees claimed that the COVID-19 pandemic had been planned and opposed the [[United Nations]]' [[Sustainable Development Goals]]. This protest breached the Alert Level 3 restrictions on mass gatherings in Auckland.<ref>{{cite news |title=Hundreds protest against lockdowns, vaccines while unmasked in Auckland |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/hundreds-protest-against-lockdowns-vaccines-while-unmasked-in-auckland |accessdate=29 August 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=29 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200829032613/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/hundreds-protest-against-lockdowns-vaccines-while-unmasked-in-auckland |archivedate=29 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 5 September, several anti-lockdown protests were held throughout the country including Auckland, [[Whangārei]], [[Wellington]], [[New Plymouth]], [[Tauranga]], [[Rotorua]], [[Nelson, New Zealand|Nelson]] and [[Christchurch]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Bayer |first1=Kurt |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Hundreds turn out for anti-lockdown protests |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12362504 |accessdate=5 September 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=5 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200905093331/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12362504 |archivedate=5 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 12 September, the Advance NZ party and Liberty March movement staged a "National Rally for Freedom" in Auckland's [[Aotea Square]] which was attended by thousands of people, including Advanced NZ party co-leaders Te Kahika and Ross. This protest breached Auckland's Alert Level 2.5 ban on gatherings of more than ten persons.<ref>{{Cite news|title=Tightly packed crowds of people descend on Auckland CBD for anti-lockdown protest|language=en-NZ|work=[[1 News]]|url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/tightly-packed-crowds-people-descend-auckland-cbd-anti-lockdown-protest|access-date=2020-09-12|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200912053040/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/tightly-packed-crowds-people-descend-auckland-cbd-anti-lockdown-protest|archive-date=2020-09-12|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|title=Anti-lockdown protestors take over Auckland's Aotea Square in 'Rally for Freedom'|language=en|work=[[Newshub]]|url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/anti-lockdown-protestors-take-over-auckland-s-aotea-square-in-rally-for-freedom.html|access-date=2020-09-12|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200912044022/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/anti-lockdown-protestors-take-over-auckland-s-aotea-square-in-rally-for-freedom.html|archive-date=2020-09-12}}</ref><ref name="National Rally 12 Sep 2020">{{cite news |title=Advance Party and crowd rallies against Covid-19 restrictions and lockdowns |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12364413 |accessdate=13 September 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=12 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200913022813/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12364413 |archivedate=13 September 2020}}</ref>

On 10 October, the Advance NZ party led by MP Ross staged a "Rally for your Future" in Auckland's Aotea Square. The NZ Liberty Movement, which had previously organised rallies with Advance NZ, did not participate due to a lack of communication and collaboration with the latter.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Palmer |first1=Scott |title=Conspiracy theorists, anti-COVID-19 'freedom fighters' march through Auckland |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/10/conspiracy-theorists-anti-covid-19-freedom-fighters-march-through-auckland.html |accessdate=10 October 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=10 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201010050840/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/10/conspiracy-theorists-anti-covid-19-freedom-fighters-march-through-auckland.html |archivedate=10 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Education sector responses===
====Primary and secondary schools====
On 17 March, [[Logan Park High School]] in Dunedin closed for 48 hours after one of its students tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref name="Stuff 12th case">{{cite news |last1=Sherwood |first1=Sam |title=Dunedin student 12th positive coronavirus case – high school to close |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120349877/dunedin-man-11th-positive-coronavirus-case |accessdate=17 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=17 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317064939/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120349877/dunedin-man-11th-positive-coronavirus-case |archive-date=17 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="ODT 12th case">{{cite news |title=Pupil tests positive, school to close |url=https://www.odt.co.nz/news/dunedin/pupil-tests-positive-school-close |accessdate=17 March 2020 |work=[[Otago Daily Times]] |date=17 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317064940/https://www.odt.co.nz/news/dunedin/pupil-tests-positive-school-close |archive-date=17 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 23 March, several schools in Auckland including [[Marist College, Auckland|Marist College]], [[Randwick Park School]] and [[Glendowie College]] closed after several teachers and parents tested positive for the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Moodie |first1=Kim |title=Coronavirus: Four Auckland schools linked to Covid-19 in one day |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318898 |accessdate=23 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=23 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200323000321/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318898 |archive-date=23 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Auckland school closing after staff member tests positive for Covid-19 |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412342/auckland-school-closing-after-staff-member-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |accessdate=23 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=23 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200322134020/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/412342/auckland-school-closing-after-staff-member-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |archive-date=22 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> That same day, the Teaching Council of Aotearoa New Zealand called on the Government to shut down all schools immediately.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Tapaleao |first1=Vaimoana |title=Coronavirus: Teachers call on Prime Minister Jacinda Ardern to shut down schools now |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318948 |accessdate=23 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=23 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200322232034/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318948 |archive-date=22 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> In response to a spike of cases and the upgrading of New Zealand's coronavirus Alert Level to Level 3, the Government closed down all schools and early childhood centres.<ref name="NZH 23 March">{{cite news |last1=Wade |first1=Amelia |title=Coronavirus lockdown: What it means for schools, universities and other education facilities |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12319139 |accessdate=24 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=23 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324001321/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12319139 |archive-date=24 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 13 May, Education Minister Chris Hipkins announced that the end-of-year high school [[National Certificate of Educational Achievement]] (NCEA) external exams would be postponed from 6 to 16 November 2020.<ref name="The Spinoff 13 May 2020" />

On 26 August, Auckland's Secondary Principals' Association announced that secondary schools were planning catch-up classes and holiday lessons for students whose education had been affected by the city's lockdown.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Gerritsen |first1=John |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Auckland students 'disadvantaged by lockdown', schools planning catch-up classes |url=https://nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12359606 |accessdate=28 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=26 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200827191919/https://nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12359606 |archivedate=27 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 8 September, [[St Dominic's Catholic College]] in Auckland's [[Henderson, New Zealand|Henderson]] suburb announced that it would shut down for a "deep clean" for three days after it was reported that a student tested positive for [[COVID-19]] that same day.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Sadler |first1=Rachel |title=Coronavirus: West Auckland school closes after confirming positive case |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-west-auckland-school-closes-after-confirming-positive-case.html |accessdate=8 September 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=8 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200908090729/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-west-auckland-school-closes-after-confirming-positive-case.html |archivedate=8 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 16 September, Chapel Downs Primary School in Auckland's [[Manukau]] suburb closed for the rest of the week after a student tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Sadler |first1=Rachel |title=Coronavirus: South Auckland school closed after student diagnosed with COVID-19 |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-south-auckland-school-closed-after-student-diagnosed-with-covid-19.html |accessdate=18 September 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=16 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200918101022/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-south-auckland-school-closed-after-student-diagnosed-with-covid-19.html |archivedate=16 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 9 November, [[Otorohanga College]] closed down its hostel after health authorities confirmed that a traveler from Wellington who had tested positive for COVID-19 had visited the facility while traveling through [[Otorohanga]] and [[Kawhia]] in the [[Waikato]] region.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Positive case on Wellington-Auckland flight; school hostel, hotel closed |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-positive-case-on-wellington-auckland-flight-school-hostel-hotel-closed/JCNH5NTZM6MFPGVWVX4WHGTJYU/ |accessdate=9 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=9 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201109025217/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-positive-case-on-wellington-auckland-flight-school-hostel-hotel-closed/JCNH5NTZM6MFPGVWVX4WHGTJYU/ |archivedate=9 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Universities and tertiary providers====
On 17 March, the [[University of Canterbury]] became the first university in New Zealand to recall its exchange students from overseas, stating that "Given the rapidly escalating global situation and the increasing amount of travel restrictions worldwide, and intensive consultation with our partners, [we have] made the very difficult decision to suspend our exchange programmes and recall all UC outbound exchange students, effective immediately."<ref>{{Cite news|last=Collins|first=Simon|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12317525|title=Coronavirus in NZ: University of Canterbury recalls exchange students from overseas|date=17 March 2020|work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |access-date=20 March 2020|language=en-NZ|issn=1170-0777|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320000926/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12317525|archive-date=20 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 20 March, [[Massey University]] stopped face-to-face teaching of courses that could be [[Distance education|taught by distance]].<ref name=Wiltshire20th>{{cite news |last1=Wiltshire |first1=Laura |last2=Keogh |first2=Brittany |title=Coronavirus: Massey and Auckland universities suspend face-to-face teaching |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120430083/massey-university-suspends-face-to-face-teaching |accessdate=20 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320011931/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120430083/massey-university-suspends-face-to-face-teaching |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The [[University of Auckland]] suspended classes for the week of 23–27 March to allow staff to prepare for remote teaching in the event of a partial campus closure.<ref>{{cite web |url= https://www.auckland.ac.nz/en/news/notices/2020/teaching-free-week.html |title=Message from the Vice-Chancellor on Teaching Free Week and possible campus closure |first=Dawn |last=Freshwater |date=20 March 2020 |publisher=University of Auckland |accessdate=21 March 2020 |url-status=live |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200320224309/https://www.auckland.ac.nz/en/news/notices/2020/teaching-free-week.html |archive-date=20 March 2020}}</ref><ref name=Wiltshire20th/> The [[University of Otago]] in [[Dunedin]] has also shifted classes with more than 100 students online while students at the University of Canterbury have petitioned for all classes to be moved online.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Sherwood |first1=Sam |title=Coronavirus: University of Otago moving classes online |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120461294/coronavirus-university-of-otago-moving-classes-online |accessdate=21 March 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321040753/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120461294/coronavirus-university-of-otago-moving-classes-online |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 21 March, [[Auckland University of Technology]] announced that it would be suspending teaching in response to a petition from students.<ref>{{cite news |title=AUT responds to student petition by closing for a week to prepare for online learning |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/aut-responds-student-petition-closing-week-prepare-online-learning |accessdate=21 March 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321040543/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/aut-responds-student-petition-closing-week-prepare-online-learning |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The [[University of Canterbury]] also announced they could move to online learning.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Mead |first=Thomas |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/canterbury-university-makes-abrupt-u-turn-and-cancels-face-lectures |title=Canterbury University makes abrupt U-turn and cancels face-to-face lectures |date=21 March 2020 |work=TVNZ |access-date=21 March 2020 |language=en-NZ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321090111/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/canterbury-university-makes-abrupt-u-turn-and-cancels-face-lectures |archive-date=21 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 23 March, all universities suspended physical lectures and shifted to online learning in response to the Government's imposition of an Alert level 3 lockdown.<ref name="NZH 23 March" />

On 14 April, the Government released a tertiary support package but it was considered unsatisfactory by tertiary students and student associations.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19: PM Jacinda Ardern announces tertiary student support package |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121006941/covid19-prime-minister-jacinda-ardern-to-announce-tertiary-student-support-package 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Several university halls of residence including [[Victoria University of Wellington]] and the University of Otago were criticised for continuing to charge rent from students, who had left their accommodation during the lockdown to isolate with their families.<ref>{{cite news |title= Victoria University halls charging rent despite locking students out |url= accommodation.<ref>{{cite web |title=Inquiry into student accommodation 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200628143740/https://www.parliament.nz/en/pb/sc/make-a-submission/document/52SCEW_SCF_INQ_98038/inquiry-into-student-accommodation|archive-date=28 June 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

In September 2020, the University of Auckland Vice-Chancellor [[Dawn Freshwater]] announced plans to resume on-campus teaching on 21 September. Following criticism from Director-General Bloomfield and students, the University retracted its decision and delayed plans to resume on-campus teaching until 5 October 2020.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Leakey |first1=Cameron |title=University of Auckland reverses decision on campus teaching at level 2.5 |url=https://thespinoff.co.nz/auckland/17-09-2020/university-of-auckland-reverses-decision-on-campus-teaching-at-level-2-5/ |accessdate=20 September 2020 |work=[[The Spinoff]] |date=20 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200920101220/https://thespinoff.co.nz/auckland/17-09-2020/university-of-auckland-reverses-decision-on-campus-teaching-at-level-2-5/ |archivedate=20 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Sadler |first1=Rachel |title=Coronavirus: University of Auckland should know physical distancing, gatherings rules before in-person learning returns - Dr Ashley Bloomfield |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-university-of-auckland-should-know-physical-distancing-gatherings-rules-before-in-person-learning-returns-dr-ashley-bloomfield.html |accessdate=20 September 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=16 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200920101823/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/09/coronavirus-university-of-auckland-should-know-physical-distancing-gatherings-rules-before-in-person-learning-returns-dr-ashley-bloomfield.html |archivedate=20 September 2020}}</ref>

On 12 October 2020, the Education Minister [[Chris Hipkins]] announced that the Government would be introducing a new border exemption allowing 250 international PhD and postgraduate students to enter New Zealand. These students will undergo the two-week mandatory quarantine.<ref name="1 News border exemption 12 Oct 2020">{{cite news |title=New border exemption sees some international students allowed back into NZ |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/new-border-exemption-sees-some-international-students-allowed-back-into-nz |accessdate=12 October 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=12 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201012041838/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/new-border-exemption-sees-some-international-students-allowed-back-into-nz |archivedate=12 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 11 November, the New Zealand Police confirmed that they were investigating an anonymous post on the controversial social media platform [[8Chan]] by an individual claiming that they were seeking to deliberately spread COVID-19 among students taking their final year exams at the University of Auckland.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Police and Auckland University investigating claims of 'superspreader' |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-police-and-auckland-university-investigating-claims-of-superspreader/ZEJLGZDY3SYOQUJPWV5PSPUOJQ/ |accessdate=12 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=11 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201110234945/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-police-and-auckland-university-investigating-claims-of-superspreader/ZEJLGZDY3SYOQUJPWV5PSPUOJQ/ |archivedate=10 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 12 November, the University of Auckland shifted all exams at its Auckland Central campuses (City, Grafton, Newmarket, and Epsom) scheduled for Friday online following the discovery of a community transmission in the city centre.<ref>{{cite news |title=University of Auckland moves Friday's exams online |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/430490/university-of-auckland-moves-friday-s-exams-online |accessdate=12 November 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=12 November 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201112094938/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/430490/university-of-auckland-moves-friday-s-exams-online|archive-date=12 November 2020}}</ref>

===Animal welfare===
On 15 April, ''[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]]'' reported that many pets included cats and dogs were stuck in transit at pet shipping companies and animal homes due to the disruption of travel caused by the coronavirus pandemic and lockdown in New Zealand. Due to lockdown restrictions, the transportation of pets is not deemed an essential service. [[Air New Zealand]] has announced that it would consider reopening its pet transportation service when Level 4 lockdown restrictions were lifted.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Kenny |first1=Jake |title=Coronavirus: Pets stuck in lockdown can't go home to owners |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/121013028/coronavirus-pets-stuck-in-lockdown-cant-go-home-to-owners |accessdate=15 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=15 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415074734/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/121013028/coronavirus-pets-stuck-in-lockdown-cant-go-home-to-owners |archivedate=15 April 2020}}</ref>

=== Court rulings ===
On 4 May, a High Court judge allowed a man who had travelled from the United Kingdom to visit his dying father, overruling the Government's strict lockdown orders including a 14-day quarantine period for all overseas travellers. In response, Prime Minister Ardern asked Health Minister David Clark to review 24 cases where health authorities blocked requests by individuals to see their dying relatives on health grounds.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Hurley |first1=Sam |last2=Bayer |first2=Kurt |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Judge overrules lockdown and allows son to visit dying dad, PM orders review of refusals |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12329451 |accessdate=5 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=5 May 2020 |archiveurl= https://web.archive.org/web/20200504100418/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12329451 |archivedate=4 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Gower |first1=Patrick |title=Coronavirus: Jacinda Ardern orders review into quarantined people wanting exemption to visit dying relatives |url= https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/05/coronavirus-jacinda-ardern-orders-review-into-quarantined-people-wanting-exemption-to-visit-dying-relatives.html |accessdate=5 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=4 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200505053339/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/05/coronavirus-jacinda-ardern-orders-review-into-quarantined-people-wanting-exemption-to-visit-dying-relatives.html |archivedate=5 May 2020}}</ref> As a result of the Government's review, a woman was granted exemption from the mandatory 14-day quarantine to visit her 59 year old terminally ill mother.<ref>{{cite news |last1=O'Brien |first1=Tova |title=Kiwi in quarantine granted exemption to see dying mother |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/kiwi-in-quarantine-granted-exemption-to-see-dying-mother.html |accessdate=7 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=6 May 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200507051614/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/kiwi-in-quarantine-granted-exemption-to-see-dying-mother.html |archive-date=7 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 19 August, the Wellington High Court ruled that the Government's message to stay at home at the start of the Alert Level 4 lockdown for nine days between 26 March and 3 April was justified but unlawful and contrary to the [[New Zealand Bill of Rights Act 1990]].  A law change on 3 April made the lockdown legal. The High Court's ruling had come in response to a legal challenge mounted by lawyer Andrew Borrowdale. The [[Attorney General (New Zealand)|Attorney General]] [[David Parker (New Zealand politician)|David Parker]] has defended the Government's handling of the lockdown and not ruled out an appeal against the ruling.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Nichol-Williams |first1=Kate |title=Early stages of Covid-19 Level 4 lockdown ruled unlawful by High Court |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/early-stages-covid-19-level-4-lockdown-ruled-unlawful-high-court |accessdate=19 August 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=19 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200819103647/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/early-stages-covid-19-level-4-lockdown-ruled-unlawful-high-court |archivedate=19 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Mitchell |first1=Jonathan |title=High Court rules some of Covid-19 level 4 lockdown was unlawful |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/423917/high-court-rules-some-of-covid-19-level-4-lockdown-was-unlawful |accessdate=19 August 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=19 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200819105019/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/423917/high-court-rules-some-of-covid-19-level-4-lockdown-was-unlawful |archivedate=19 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Vaccines===
In late August 2020 [[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] reported that several businessmen and former politicians (including former [[New Zealand National Party|National]] MP [[Ross Meurant]] and former National Party and [[ACT New Zealand|ACT party]] leader [[Don Brash]]) had sought to import Russia's insufficiently tested [[Gam-COVID-Vac]] (also known as Sputnik V) vaccine into New Zealand. They had established a company called Covax-NZR Limited and filed paperwork through the Russian Embassy to establish supply and distribution arrangements to import the vaccine. [[University of Auckland]] vaccinologist [[Helen Petousis-Harris]] warned that using untested vaccines could hurt global efforts to develop safe and effective vaccines against COVID-19.<ref>
{{cite news |last1= Shand |first1= Matt |title= Coronavirus: Kiwis push Kremlin to import unproven Covid-19 vaccine |url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300094032/coronavirus-kiwis-push-kremlin-to-import-unproven-covid19-vaccine |accessdate= 30 August 2020 |work= [[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date= 30 August 2020 |url-status= live |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200901230617/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300094032/coronavirus-kiwis-push-kremlin-to-import-unproven-covid19-vaccine |archive-date= 30 August 2020}}
</ref>

On 12 October 2020, the Government signed an agreement with [[Pfizer]] and [[BioNTech]] to buy 1.5 million COVID-19 vaccines, which is enough for 750,000 people. The COVID-19 Vaccine Strategy Task Force is also negotiating with other pharmaceutical companies to provide vaccines. In addition, the Government has established a fund of $66.3 million to support a COVID-19 immunisation programme as soon as the vaccine is ready.<ref>{{cite news |title=Government signs agreement to purchase 1.5m Covid-19 vaccines, enough for 750k people |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/government-signs-agreement-purchase-1-5m-covid-19-vaccines-enough-750k-people |accessdate=12 October 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=12 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201012041410/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/government-signs-agreement-purchase-1-5m-covid-19-vaccines-enough-750k-people |archivedate=12 October 2020}}</ref>

=== Public opinion ===

==== Government response approval ====
An Utting Research poll conducted on 1–2 March found that 47% of respondents were satisfied with the government's overall response to the COVID-19 outbreak, with 34% unsatisfied and 19% unsure.<ref name="poll1">{{Cite news|last1=Cooke|first1=Henry|last2=Malpass|first2=Luke|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/politics/120003679/coronavirus-kiwis-want-more-border-control-dont-think-govt-can-stop-outbreak|title=Coronavirus: Kiwis want more border control, don't think Govt can stop outbreak|work=Stuff|date=5 March 2020|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305170956/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/politics/120003679/coronavirus-kiwis-want-more-border-control-dont-think-govt-can-stop-outbreak|archive-date=5 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> A subsequent poll conducted on 21–22 March, prior to the lockdown announcement, found that 62% of respondents were satisfied with the response.<ref name="poll2">{{Cite news|last1=Cooke|first1=Henry|last2=Malpass|first2=Luke|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120534052/coronavirus-poll-shows-kiwis-back-harsh-measures-but-are-extremely-worried-about-virus|title=Coronavirus: Poll shows Kiwis back harsh measures but are extremely worried about virus|website=Stuff|date=25 March 2020|access-date=25 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324234129/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120534052/coronavirus-poll-shows-kiwis-back-harsh-measures-but-are-extremely-worried-about-virus|archive-date=24 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> However, 37% were not confident a large-scale outbreak could be prevented in New Zealand, with 26% confident and 36% unsure.<ref name="poll2" />

A ''[[Newshub]]''-Reid Research poll conducted from 8 to 16 May 2020 asked whether it was "the right call" to implement the March–April nationwide Level 4 stay-at-home order. 91.6% responded "yes", 6% "no" and 2.5% "don't know".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/05/newshub-reid-research-poll-overwhelming-number-of-kiwis-back-government-s-lockdown-decision.html |title=Newshub-Reid Research Poll: Overwhelming number of Kiwis back Government's lockdown decision |first=Jenna |last=Lynch |work=[[Newshub]] |date=18 May 2020 |accessdate=18 May 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200521224142/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/05/newshub-reid-research-poll-overwhelming-number-of-kiwis-back-government-s-lockdown-decision.html |archive-date=21 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 9 August, a Horizon Research poll found that trust in the Ministry of Health and Government's ability to manage the COVID-19 pandemic was 82%, down from 91% in April 2020. The poll also found that 64% of New Zealanders still "totally" trusted the Government and Ministry of Health, down from 75% in April.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: New Zealanders' trust in Government's pandemic management falls |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12354876 |accessdate=9 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=9 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200809035034/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12354876 |archivedate=9 August 2020}}</ref>

==== Media perception ====
Due to the large viewing of the daily 1&nbsp;pm press briefings, the actions of and lines of questioning from journalists came under scrutiny from the public, with many criticising repetitive or aggressive lines of questioning and "gotcha" accusations. [[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] journalist Thomas Coughlan replied that the criticism "seemed to come from nowhere" and these actions are "really the way it's always been", saying that the methodology has only come into question due to the large viewership of the press conferences.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.newsroom.co.nz/podcast-the-detail/the-1pm-news-scramble|title=The 1pm news scramble|first=Sharon|last=Brettkelly|work=Newsroom|date=2020-09-15|accessdate=2020-09-16}}</ref> Television producer Robyn Patterson, writing for ''[[Newsroom]]'', commented that the "aggressive stance of some local journalists ... is leading to a public backlash", which "elevates the anxiety levels of an already distressed public and creates deep unease". She noted that a 2019 [[Griffith University]] study of journalistic best practice recommended that journalists consider the needs of those impacted by disastrous events or else they risk to cause more harm than good.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.newsroom.co.nz/robyn-paterson-oped|title=The watchdog role of our journalists|first=Robyn|last=Patterson|website=Newsroom|date=2020-09-05|accessdate=2020-09-16}}</ref>

===International responses===
On 8 September, the Secretary-General of the [[World Health Organization]] Dr [[Tedros Adhanom]] praised New Zealand's response to the COVID-19 pandemic alongside several other countries including Cambodia, Japan, South Korea, Rwanda, Senegal, Spain, and Vietnam.<ref>{{cite news |title=World Health Organization praises New Zealand's response to Covid-19 again |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/world-health-organization-praises-new-zealands-response-covid-19-again |accessdate=17 October 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=17 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200908020020/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/world-health-organization-praises-new-zealands-response-covid-19-again |archivedate=17 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 28 October, [[Hoover Institution]] senior fellow [[Victor Davis Hanson]] criticised Prime Minister Ardern's requirement that people undergoing managed isolation quarantine be tested as a condition for leaving on [[Fox News]]'s ''[[The Ingraham Angle]]'' while the show's host [[Laura Ingraham]] likened MIQ facilities to coronavirus "quarantine camps".<ref>{{cite news |last1=Creitz |first1=Charles |title=Victor Davis Hanson laments New Zealand's COVID-19 quarantine 'camps' as end of personal freedom |url=https://www.foxnews.com/world/victor-davis-hanson-new-zealand-coronavirus-camps |accessdate=29 October 2020 |work=[[Fox News]] |date=28 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201028180357/https://www.foxnews.com/world/victor-davis-hanson-new-zealand-coronavirus-camps |archivedate=28 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Hanson and [[Laura Ingraham]] drew coverage from New Zealand media commentators including ''[[The Spinoff]]''{{'s}} Alex Braee, who compared their remarks to former [[United Kingdom Independence Party]] politician [[Suzanne Evans]]' remarks likening New Zealand's lockdown policies to [[Nazi Germany]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Braae |first1=Alex |title=The Bulletin: Idiots abroad infuriated by NZ's Covid response |url=https://thespinoff.co.nz/the-bulletin/29-10-2020/the-bulletin-idiots-abroad-infuriated-by-nzs-covid-response/ |accessdate=29 October 2020 |work=[[The Spinoff]] |date=29 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201029005643/https://thespinoff.co.nz/the-bulletin/29-10-2020/the-bulletin-idiots-abroad-infuriated-by-nzs-covid-response/ |archivedate=29 October 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> [[Newshub]]'s Jamie Ensor responded that Ingraham's comments lacked context, explaining that the camps were actually lavish hotels and motels.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Ensor |first1=Jamie |title=Who is Laura Ingraham? A look at the Fox News host whose 'quarantine camps' comments shocked NZ |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/world/2020/10/who-is-laura-ingraham-a-look-at-the-fox-news-host-whose-quarantine-camps-comments-shocked-nz.html |accessdate=29 October 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201029005828/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/world/2020/10/who-is-laura-ingraham-a-look-at-the-fox-news-host-whose-quarantine-camps-comments-shocked-nz.html |archivedate=29 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

== Long-term effects ==
In April 2020, the [[New Zealand Treasury]] projected that the country could experience an unemployment rate of 13.5% if the country remained in lockdown for four weeks, with a range of between 17.5% and 26% if the lockdown was extended.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Walls|first=Jason|date=14 April 2020|title=Jobless rate could reach 26% if lockdown extended, according to the Treasury|work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12324544|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200831192417/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12324544|archive-date=31 August 2020|access-date=16 May 2020|issn=1170-0777|url-status=live}}</ref> Prior to the lockdown, the unemployment rate was at 4.2%.<ref>{{cite web|title=Unemployment rate {{!}} Stats NZ|url=https://www.stats.govt.nz/indicators/unemployment-rate|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200516015219/https://www.stats.govt.nz/indicators/unemployment-rate|url-status=dead|archive-date=16 May 2020|date=16 May 2020|access-date=16 May 2020}}</ref> Finance Minister [[Grant Robertson]] vowed that the Government would keep the unemployment rate below 10%.<ref>{{cite web|title=Coronavirus: Treasury models paint dire economic picture, mass unemployment {{!}} Stuff.co.nz|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/120995116/coronavirus-treasury-models-paint-dire-economic-picture-mass-unemployment|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200413224437/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/120995116/coronavirus-treasury-models-paint-dire-economic-picture-mass-unemployment|url-status=dead|archive-date=13 April 2020|date=13 April 2020|access-date=16 May 2020}}</ref>

In the second quarter of 2020, unemployment fell 0.2 percentage points to 4 percent; however, the under-utilization rate (a measure of spare capacity in the labor market) rose to a record 12 percent, up 1.6 percentage points from the previous quarter, and working hours fell by 10 percent.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Hargreaves |first1=David |title=Statistics New Zealand says unemployment rate actually FELL to 4%, but the 'underutilisation' rate had a record climb, up to 12%, employment fell by 11,000 jobs and 37,000 people left the workforce |url=https://www.interest.co.nz/news/106378/statistics-new-zealand-says-unemployment-rate-actually-fell-4-underutilisation-rate-had |accessdate=4 September 2020 |work=Interest.co.nz |date=5 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200807022849/https://www.interest.co.nz/news/106378/statistics-new-zealand-says-unemployment-rate-actually-fell-4-underutilisation-rate-had |archivedate=7 August 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref>

National GDP contracted 1.6% in the first quarter of 2020.<ref>{{Cite news|title=Covid-19 took 1.6 per cent chunk out of GDP by end of March|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/300037447/covid19-took-16-per-cent-chunk-out-of-gdp-by-end-of-march|date=17 June 2020|access-date=18 June 2020|website=Stuff}}</ref> The country officially entered a [[recession]] in September after [[Statistics New Zealand]] reported a GDP contraction of 12.2% in the second quarter of 2020.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/122796028/nz-in-recession-as-covid-shrinks-gdp-by-122|title=NZ in recession as Covid shrinks GDP by 12.2%|first=Tom|last=Pullar-Strecker|work=Stuff|publisher=[[Stuff Ltd]]|date=2020-09-17|accessdate=2020-09-17}}</ref> The second-quarter contraction was lead by a 47.4% contraction in accommodation and food and beverage services, a 38.7% contraction in transport, postal and warehousing, and a 25.8% contaction in construction.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Gross domestic product: June 2020 quarter {{!}} Stats NZ|url=https://www.stats.govt.nz/information-releases/gross-domestic-product-june-2020-quarter|access-date=2020-09-28|website=www.stats.govt.nz}}</ref>

On 4 November 2020, [[Statistics New Zealand]] reported that the unemployment rate had risen to 5.3% as a result of COVID-19, with the number of unemployed increasing by 37,000 to reach 151,000.<ref>{{cite web |title=Unemployment rate hits 5.3 percent due to COVID-19 |url=https://www.stats.govt.nz/news/unemployment-rate-hits-5-3-percent-due-to-covid-19 |publisher=[[Statistics New Zealand]] |accessdate=7 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201103215350/https://www.stats.govt.nz/news/unemployment-rate-hits-5-3-percent-due-to-covid-19 |archivedate=4 November 2020 |date=4 November 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref>

== Alert level system ==
On 21 March, [[Prime Minister of New Zealand|Prime Minister]] [[Jacinda Ardern]] announced the introduction of a country-wide alert level system, similar to the existing fire warning systems. There are four levels, with 1 being the least risk of infection and 4 the highest. At the time of the announcement, New Zealand was at Level 2. Each level brings added restrictions on activities or movements. Each region can have an individual alert level based on the severity of their own infections, and these levels can be changed at any time.<ref name="Unite against COVID-19">{{Cite web|url=https://covid19.govt.nz/|title=Home|website=Unite against COVID-19|access-date=21 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321091125/http://covid19.govt.nz/|archive-date=21 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="NZH 21 Mar 20">{{Cite news|last=Cheng|first=Derek|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318673|title=Coronavirus: PM Jacinda Ardern outlines NZ's new alert system, over-70s should stay at home|date=20 March 2020|work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |access-date=21 March 2020|language=en-NZ|issn=1170-0777|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200321113000/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12318673|archive-date=21 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

At the time of Ardern's announcement, New Zealand was at Alert Level 2.<ref>{{cite news |last1=O'Brien |first1=Tova |title=Jacinda Ardern announces alert system for COVID-19 |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/jacinda-ardern-announces-alert-system-for-covid-19.html |accessdate=21 April 2020 |work=Newshub |date=21 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407184703/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/03/jacinda-ardern-announces-alert-system-for-covid-19.html |archive-date=7 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Ardern announced on 23 March that, effective immediately, New Zealand would be at Alert Level 3, moving to Level 4 at 11:59&nbsp;pm on 25 March.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120495548/live-pm-jacinda-ardern-to-give-update-on-coronavirus-alert-level|title=Live: PM Jacinda Ardern to give update on coronavirus alert level|website=Stuff|language=en|access-date=23 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200323005056/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120495548/live-pm-jacinda-ardern-to-give-update-on-coronavirus-alert-level|archive-date=23 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> On 20 April, Ardern announced that New Zealand would move to Alert Level 3 at 11:59&nbsp;pm on 27 April, with businesses and schools being allowed to have employees enter the premises during the last week of Alert Level 4 to prepare the facility for the transition to Alert Level 3.<ref name="Level 3 Stuff">{{cite news|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121131785/coronavirus-prime-minister-jacinda-ardern-will-reveal-alert-level-three-decision-at-4pm|title=Coronavirus: Prime Minister Jacinda Ardern says NZ will stay in lockdown until April 27|first1=Collette|last1=Devlin|first2=Henry|last2=Cooke|work=Stuff|date=20 April 2020|accessdate=20 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200420135304/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121131785/coronavirus-prime-minister-jacinda-ardern-will-reveal-alert-level-three-decision-at-4pm|archive-date=20 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> The country remained at Alert Level 3 for at least two weeks, with the decision of whether to move down to Level 2 made on 11 May.<ref name="Level 3 Newshub">{{cite news|url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/04/coronavirus-lockdown-in-new-zealand-to-end-in-a-week-as-nation-will-shift-into-covid-19-alert-level-3.html|title=Coronavirus lockdown in New Zealand to end in a week as nation will shift into COVID-19 alert level 3|first=Zane|last=Small|work=Newshub|date=20 April 2020|accessdate=20 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200422234619/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/04/coronavirus-lockdown-in-new-zealand-to-end-in-a-week-as-nation-will-shift-into-covid-19-alert-level-3.html|archive-date=22 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> On 11 May, it was announced that New Zealand would enter Alert Level 2 from 11:59&nbsp;pm on 13 May, lifting lockdown restrictions while maintaining physical distancing in public and for private gatherings with more than ten people.<ref name="Stuff 11 May Level 2"/> On 8 June, Ardern announced that the country would enter Alert Level 1 at 11:59&nbsp;pm that night, lifting the remaining restrictions.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300029276/recap-new-zealand-will-move-to-covid19-alert-level-1 |title=Live: New Zealand will move to Covid-19 Alert Level 1|work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]]|date=8 June 2020|accessdate=8 June 2020 |url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200801070214/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300029276/recap-new-zealand-will-move-to-covid19-alert-level-1|archive-date=1 August 2020}}</ref> After new cases of community transmission were detected on 11 August, New Zealand was moved to Alert Level 2 and Auckland to Level 3 at noon on 12 August;<ref name="NZH Auckland lockdown"/> Auckland moved down to Level "2.5", a modified version of Level 2 with further limitations on public gatherings and mandated mask wearing on public transport, at 11:59&nbsp;pm on 30 August.<ref name="Cardwell"/> New Zealand moved to Level 1 on 21 September at 11:59&nbsp;pm while Auckland moved to Level 2 on 23 September at 11:59&nbsp;pm.<ref name="The New Zealand Herald"/> Auckland moved down to Level 1 on 7 October at 11:59&nbsp;pm.<ref name="Auckland Level 1 Oct 7"/>

=== Alert levels ===

Alert levels are cumulative – each level includes the restrictions of the level below it. The levels are as follows:<ref>{{cite web|url=https://covid19.govt.nz/alert-system/covid-19-alert-system/|title=COVID-19 Alert System in New Zealand|last=|first=|date=16 April 2020|website=covid19.govt.nz|publisher=New Zealand Government|accessdate=16 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200415140052/https://covid19.govt.nz/alert-system/covid-19-alert-system/|archive-date=15 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>
{| class="wikitable"
!No.
!Name
!Description and Measures
|-
!<big>1</big>
|Prepare
|COVID-19 is uncontrolled overseas. The disease is contained in New Zealand and there are sporadic imported cases, but isolated household transmission could be occurring.

*Border entry measures to minimise risk of importing COVID-19 cases.
*Intensive testing for COVID-19.
*Rapid [[contact tracing]] of any positive case.
*People arriving in New Zealand without symptoms of COVID-19 go into a managed [[Isolation (health care)|isolation]] facility for at least 14 days.<ref name="MOH_MI&Q">{{cite web|date=3 July 2020|title=COVID-19 – Managed isolation and quarantine|url=https://www.health.govt.nz/our-work/diseases-and-conditions/covid-19-novel-coronavirus/covid-19-current-situation/covid-19-border-controls/covid-19-managed-isolation-and-quarantine|accessdate=10 July 2020|publisher=Ministry of Health}}</ref>
*People arriving in New Zealand with symptoms of COVID-19 or who test positive after arrival go into a quarantine facility and are unable to leave their room for at least 14 days.<ref name="MOH_MI&Q" />
*Mandatory [[Isolation (health care)|self-isolation]] may be applied.
*Schools and workplaces are open, and must operate safely.
*No restrictions on personal movement or gatherings.
*Stay home if you are sick, report flu-like symptoms.
*Wash and dry hands, cough into elbow, do not touch your face.
*No restrictions on domestic transport – avoid public transport or travel if sick.
*Businesses and public transport must display QR codes to allow for contact tracing.
|-
!<big>2</big>
|Reduce
|The disease is contained, but the risk of community transmission remains. Household transmission could be occurring, and there are single or isolated cluster outbreaks.

*People can connect with friends and family, go shopping, or travel domestically, but should follow public health guidance.
*Physical distancing of two metres from people you do not know when out in public is recommended, with one metre physical distancing in controlled environments like workplaces unless other measures are in place.
*No more than 100 people at indoor or outdoor gatherings (subject to any lower limit, e.g. fire regulations).
*Sport and recreation activities are allowed, subject to conditions on gatherings, contact tracing, and – where practical – physical distancing.
*Public venues can open but must comply with public health measures.
*Health and disability care services operate as normally as possible.
*Businesses can open to the public, but must follow public health guidance including in relation to physical distancing and contact tracing. Alternative ways of working encouraged where possible (e.g. remote working, shift-based working, physical distancing, staggering meal breaks, flexible leave).
*Schools, early childhood education and tertiary education providers can open with appropriate public health measures in place.
*People at higher risk of severe illness from COVID-19 (e.g. those with underlying medical conditions, especially if not well controlled, and seniors) are encouraged to take additional precautions when leaving home. They may work, if they agree with their employer that they can do so safely.
*Face coverings are required on public transport and aircraft, but not school buses or Cook Strait ferries. children under 12 are exempt along with passengers in taxis or rideshare services and people with disabilities or mental health conditions.
|-
!<big>3</big>
|Restrict
|There is a high risk the disease is not contained. Community transmission might be happening. New clusters may emerge but can be controlled through testing and contact tracing.

*People instructed to stay home in their [[support bubble]] other than for essential personal movement – including to go to work, school if they have to or for local recreation. 
*Physical distancing of two metres outside home (including on public transport), or one metre In controlled environments like schools and workplaces.
*People must stay within their immediate household bubble, but can expand this to reconnect with close family / whānau, or bring in caregivers, or support isolated people. This extended bubble should remain exclusive.
*Schools (years 1 to 10) and Early Childhood Education centres can safely open, but will have limited capacity. Children should learn at home if possible.
*People must work from home unless that is not possible.
*Businesses can open premises, but cannot physically interact with customers.
*Low risk local recreation activities are allowed.
*Public venues are closed (e.g. libraries, museums, cinemas, food courts, gyms, pools, playgrounds, markets).
*Gatherings of up to 10 people are allowed but only for wedding services, funerals and tangihanga. Physical distancing and public health measures must be maintained.
*Healthcare services use virtual, non-contact consultations where possible.
*Inter-regional travel is highly limited (e.g. for essential workers, with limited exemptions for others).
*People at high risk of severe illness (older people and those with existing medical conditions) are encouraged to stay at home where possible, and take additional precautions when leaving home. They may choose to continue to work.
|-
!<big>4</big>
|Eliminate
|It is likely the disease is not contained. Sustained and intensive community transmission is occurring, and there are widespread outbreaks and new clusters.

* People must stay at home (in their bubble) other than for essential personal movement.
* Safe recreational activity is allowed in local area.
* Travel is severely limited.
* All gatherings cancelled and all public venues closed.
* Businesses closed except for [[COVID-19 pandemic in New Zealand#Essential services|essential services]] (e.g. supermarkets, pharmacies, clinics, petrol stations) and [[Lifeline utility|lifeline utilities]].
* Educational facilities closed.
* Rationing of supplies and requisitioning of facilities possible.
* Reprioritisation of healthcare services.
|}

===Essential services===
[[File:New World Supermarket During COVID-19 Pandemic.jpg|thumb|300px|Supermarket staff behind protective screens and wearing gloves on 31 March 2020]]
The "essential services" referenced in Alert Level 4 include:<ref name="Essential services">{{cite web |title=Essential businesses |url=https://covid19.govt.nz/businesses-and-employees/essential-businesses/ |date=12 April 2020 |website=covid19.govt.nz |publisher=[[New Zealand Government]] |access-date=14 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200414002409/https://covid19.govt.nz/businesses-and-employees/essential-businesses/ |archive-date=14 April 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 essential services: What remains open during a lockdown |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/covid-19/412477/covid-19-essential-services-what-remains-open-during-a-lockdown |accessdate=24 March 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=24 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324030516/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/covid-19/412477/covid-19-essential-services-what-remains-open-during-a-lockdown |archive-date=24 March 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Walls |first1=Jason |title=Covid-19 coronavirus lockdown: What is an 'essential' service that can stay open? |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12319181 |accessdate=24 March 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=24 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324001205/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12319181 |archive-date=24 March 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref>

*'''Accommodation'''
**Any entity that provides accommodation services for essential workers, isolation/quarantine, and emergency housing
**Retirement villages
*'''Border'''
**[[New Zealand Customs Service]], [[Immigration New Zealand]], and the [[Ministry for Primary Industries (New Zealand)|Ministry for Primary Industries]]
*'''Building and construction'''
**Any entity involved in building and construction related to essential services and critical infrastructure, including those in the supply and support chain
**Any entity involved in any work required to address immediate health or life safety risks, or to prevent serious environmental harm, and relevant essential supply chain elements
**Any entity with statutory responsibilities or that is involved in building and resource consenting necessary for the above purposes
*'''Courts, tribunals and the justice system'''
**[[Judiciary of New Zealand|Courts of New Zealand]], tribunals
**Critical Crown entities such as the [[Electoral Commission (New Zealand)|Electoral Commission]]
*'''Education'''
**Any entity or individual determined by the Secretary for Education as required to provide distance or online learning (e.g. printers, devices, IT)
*'''Fast-moving community goods'''
**Any entity involved in the supply, delivery, distribution and sale of food, beverage and other key consumer goods essential for maintaining the wellbeing of people
*'''Financial services'''
**Any entity that operates consumer and business financial services, financial services infrastructure (including banking services), a stock exchange, broking services, payment and settlement systems, funds management (including [[KiwiSaver]]), insurance services, financial advice, and support services such as administrators, supervisors and custodians
*'''Health'''
**[[District health board]]s (and all of their facilities), [[Pharmac]], [[New Zealand Blood Service]], Health Promotion Agency, Health Quality and Safety Commission
**Any person employed or contracted as a doctor, nurse, midwife, pharmacist, paramedic, medical laboratory scientists, kaiāwhina workers, social workers, aged-care and community workers, and caregivers more generally
**Hospitals, primary care clinics, pharmacies, medical laboratories, care facilities (e.g. rest homes)
**Emergency dental and optometry care services
**Any entity providing [[Emergency medical services in New Zealand|ambulance services]]
**Any entity involved with the deceased/tūpāpaku (e.g. funeral homes, crematoria, cemeteries)
**Any entity producing health sector equipment, medicines and [[personal protective equipment]]
*'''Local and national government'''
**Any entity involved in COVID-19 response, enforcement, planning or logistics or that has civil-defence/emergency management functions (including any entity that supplies services for these purposes)
**Key public services
*'''Foreign government'''
**Maintaining critical operations at foreign missions based in New Zealand.
*'''Primary industries, including food and beverage production and processing'''
**Any entity involved in the packaging, production and processing of food and beverage products, whether for domestic consumption or export
**Any entity involved in relevant support services, such as food safety and verification, inspection or associated laboratory services, food safety and biosecurity functions
**Any entity providing veterinary services
**Any entity whose closure would jeopardise the maintenance of animal health or welfare standards (including the short-term survival of a species)
*'''Public safety and national security'''
**[[Department of Corrections (New Zealand)|Department of Corrections]], [[Fire and Emergency New Zealand]], [[Ministry of Defence (New Zealand)|Ministry of Defence]], [[Ministry of Justice (New Zealand)|Ministry of Justice]], [[New Zealand Defence Force]], [[New Zealand Police]], [[New Zealand Security Intelligence Service]] (NZSIS), [[Government Communications Security Bureau]] (GCSB)
**Any person employed or contracted in a public safety or national security role
*'''Science'''
**[[Institute of Environmental Science and Research|ESR]], [[GNS Science]], GeoNet, [[National Institute of Water and Atmospheric Research|NIWA]], [[MetService]]
**Any entity (including research organisations) involved in COVID-19 response
**Any entity (including research organisations) involved in hazard monitoring and resilience
**Any entity (including research organisations) involved in diagnostics for essential services like biosecurity, public health
**Laboratories and Physical Containment Level 3 (PC3) facilities that could provide essential services and products that could be used to respond to COVID-19
**Other significant research facilities including animal facilities, clinical trials and infrastructure that require constant attention (e.g. samples, collections and storage facilities) that are important to New Zealand
*'''Social services'''
**Those entities, including non-government organisations, that provide welfare and social services to meet immediate needs, to be specified jointly by the [[Ministry of Social Development (New Zealand)|Ministry of Social Development]] (MSD) and [[Ministry for Children|Oranga Tamariki]]
*'''Transport and logistics'''
**[[Ministry of Transport (New Zealand)|Ministry of Transport]], [[New Zealand Customs Service]], [[NZ Transport Agency]], [[Civil Aviation Authority of New Zealand|Civil Aviation Authority]] (including Aviation Security Service), [[Maritime New Zealand]] (including the Rescue Coordination Centre), [[Airways NZ]], [[MetService]], [[KiwiRail]] (including [[Interislander]]), and any entity that is contracted by these entities
**Any entity that provides, or is contracted to an entity that provides, logistics services, including [[New Zealand Post]] and courier services
**Any entity providing, or is contracted by an entity that provides, transport services to the Ministry of Health, a District Health Board, a Medical Officer of Health, or a Controller (as defined in section 4 of the Civil Defence and Emergency Management Act 2002)
**Any entity that provides services related to the maintenance and ongoing operation of critical infrastructure (e.g. roads, rail, ports, airports)
**Any entity that operates or is contracted by a [[lifeline utility]], an aerodrome, a passenger and/or freight aviation service, a passenger and/or freight shipping service, a road freight service, a rail freight service, a vehicle recovery service; or a public transport service (under contract with a Regional Council)
**Any small passenger-service vehicle driver (who holds the relevant licence) such as ride-share or taxi drivers
**Any entity providing services to keep vehicles operational for essential work purposes (e.g. vehicle testing, mechanics, tyre services)
*'''Utilities and communications, including supply chains'''
**Any entity involved in the production, supply, sale distribution or disposal of electricity, gas, water, waste water (e.g. sanitation), waste (e.g. rubbish collection and recycling), liquid and solid fuel, telecommunication services, and any entity that is contracted by these entities
**The delivery of solid fuels (including firewood, pellets and coal) for immediate needs (e.g. home heating) or fulfilling existing orders, is an essential service.
**[[Media of New Zealand|News (including news production) and broadcast media]]
**Internet service providers
**Any entity that provides maintenance and repair services for utilities and communications, including supply chains
**Any entity supplying services to an essential workplace that are required for the safe operation of that workplace (e.g. cleaning, security services)
**Commercial cleaners that clean common areas of apartment buildings may continue to operate where there is high traffic (e.g. lifts, stairwells)
*'''Additional decisions and exemptions'''
**All supermarkets and [[Dairy (store)|dairies]] are considered an essential service. A supermarket's primary focus is selling food products, and is a retail store operating on a self-service basis, selling groceries, fresh produce, meat, bakery and dairy products, and sometimes an assortment of non-food goods. Dairies must operate a "one-in-one-out" rule, and cannot sell cooked food.
**Essential consumer products other than food (e.g. blankets, heaters, kitchenware and appliances, whiteware, computer equipment and mobile phones) may be sold subject to conditions. If a business cannot meet these conditions, it must not offer goods for sale.
**Food delivery other than cooked prepared meals such as takeaways is allowed (e.g. supermarket home delivery, food parcels from charitable organisations, subscription food boxes, or any other whole-food delivery service). Meals-on-Wheels may continue to deliver prepared food. Ordering, payment and delivery must be contactless and the business must operate safely within the general health guidelines such as physical separation and hygiene.
**Locksmiths can undertake essential work on emergency call-outs and essential activity to maintain the security of premises/personal properties.
**Turf maintenance is not considered an essential service and should not be undertaken at this time.
**Pet care services are not considered to be essential, except where necessary to maintain existing boarding of animals in pet care, or for long-term care when no other alternatives are available.
**Vehicle washing services must only be undertaken when supporting essential services to ensure they are complying with the necessary health and safety requirements (e.g. washing off contaminated or biohazard materials).
**Road safety equipment for road construction should only be used only where maintenance is essential.
**Farmers markets are not considered to be an essential service, as alternatives are available
**Liquor stores must close to the public unless they are within monopoly [[Licensing trust|Licensing Trust]] areas (i.e. West Auckland, Gore and Invercargill), in which case they can operate with a one-in-one-out rule.
**Pest management may be undertaken only where required for human health and safety, and it is essential. However, operators must ensure people have somewhere safe to go while the process is underway, in particular where a property is being vacated
**Campgrounds and backpacker accommodation providers may continue to operate under very strict protocols and management of access. (e.g. contact to be maintained only with people staying in the same abode/room; common social and recreation areas to be closed; split shift access to common areas)
**Butchers, bakeries and similar small-scale food retailers are considered non-essential, as similar products are readily available in supermarkets.
**Natural health services are considered non-essential.
**Security is considered an essential service, even if security services are being provided in relation to a premise for a non-essential service.
**Self-storage facilities can operate only to facilitate access for essentials. New sales or expiries of units are considered non-essential. Access to existing lockers is permitted for essential items or services only, e.g. fridges
**Critical support services to ensure businesses and workers can continue working from home are considered to be essential. This includes functions such as IT and Payroll.
**Every restaurant, café and bar must close all aspects of their operation.
**Self-service laundries can stay open, with 2-metre physical distancing to be enforced.
**[[Bunnings Warehouse|Bunnings]], [[PlaceMakers|Placemakers]], [[Mitre 10 (New Zealand)|Mitre 10]] and other retailers essential to the supply chain for building and construction can stay open to trade customers for essential purposes only.
**The [[Tiwai Point Aluminium Smelter]] is exempt from closure, due to the long and complicated process of closing and restarting the potlines.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120560247/coronavirus-tiwai-point-aluminium-smelter-deemed-essential-service|title=Coronavirus: Tiwai Point aluminium smelter exempted from lockdown|website=Stuff|language=en|access-date=26 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200326041750/https://www.stuff.co.nz/business/120560247/coronavirus-tiwai-point-aluminium-smelter-deemed-essential-service|archive-date=26 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>
**[[New Zealand Steel]] is to shut down in a way that allows for production to recommence easily.
**Pulp and paper plants (e.g. [[Tasman Mill|Tasman]], [[Kinleith Mill|Kinleith]]) are to shut down their non-essential elements in a way that allows for production to recommence easily, and while maintaining essential production.
**[[Methanex]] can remain in production, but at a scale consistent with the stability of gas supply.

===Lockdown violations===
Since New Zealand entered into a Level 4 alert lockdown on 25 March 2020, there have been several reports of people violating lockdown rules by congregating in crowds. On 1 April, Ardern described 20–29 year olds as the most vulnerable demographic to COVID-19 and called on them to comply with lockdown requirements.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Cooke |first1=Henry |title=Coronavirus: Jacinda Ardern unleashes on 20-somethings not taking virus seriously |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/politics/120743026/coronavirus-jacinda-ardern-unleashes-on-20somethings-not-taking-virus-seriously |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=1 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402090052/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/politics/120743026/coronavirus-jacinda-ardern-unleashes-on-20somethings-not-taking-virus-seriously |archive-date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title='Our vector of transmission' – Jacinda Ardern's fiery message to young adults not sticking to lockdown |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/our-vector-transmission-jacinda-arderns-fiery-message-young-adults-not-sticking-lockdown |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=1 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402090234/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/our-vector-transmission-jacinda-arderns-fiery-message-young-adults-not-sticking-lockdown |archive-date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 2 April, there were reports of beachgoers congregating in Auckland's [[Herne Bay, New Zealand|Herne Bay]], and [[Dunedin]]. Police have visited beachgoers, warning them to comply with the lockdown, while health authorities have warned about the risk of spreading the coronavirus and prolonging the lockdown.<ref>{{cite news |title=Auckland beachgoers caught on video, scolded for disobeying coronavirus lockdown |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/auckland-beachgoers-caught-video-scolded-disobeying-coronavirus-lockdown?auto=6146381201001 |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=2 April
