|archive-date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> In [[Otago]], there have been reports of people jumping off the Albert Town Bridge near [[Wanaka]].{{clarify|date=April 2020}}<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Group spotted jumping off Albert Town Bridge, into river during lockdown |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12322092 |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200402104641/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12322092 |archive-date=2 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> In Auckland, Tongan ethnic community leaders have also warned that [[kava]] clubs are still meeting despite the lockdown, with some participants posting photos and videos on social media.<ref>{{cite news |title=Auckland kava drinking groups continue to meet despite lockdown |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/auckland-kava-drinking-groups-continue-meet-despite-lockdown |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200405074530/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/auckland-kava-drinking-groups-continue-meet-despite-lockdown |archive-date=5 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> In [[Kaitaia]], there have been reports of locals taking matters into their own hands by establishing checkpoints to enforce the lockdown.<ref>{{cite news |title=Kaitaia area under police scrutiny as some locals flouting lockdown law |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/kaitaia-area-under-police-scrutiny-some-locals-flouting-lockdown-law?auto=6146475209001 |accessdate=2 April 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200513161333/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/kaitaia-area-under-police-scrutiny-some-locals-flouting-lockdown-law?auto=6146475209001 |archive-date=13 May 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

In early April, Health Minister [[David Clark (New Zealand politician)|David Clark]] was criticised for flouting official guidelines against non-essential travel after he drove to a Dunedin park two kilometres away from his home to ride a mountain bike trail. Clark later apologised to Prime Minister Ardern for not setting a good example to the public.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Manch |first1=Thomas |last2=Cooke |first2=Henry |title=Health Minister drives to local park to ride his mountain bike, amid coronavirus lockdown |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120780372/health-minister-drives-to-local-park-to-ride-his-mountain-bike-amid-coronavirus-lockdown |accessdate=4 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=2 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407003543/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120780372/health-minister-drives-to-local-park-to-ride-his-mountain-bike-amid-coronavirus-lockdown |archive-date=7 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus Covid 19: David Clark apologises to PM for flouting his own Government's lockdown advice |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12322301 |accessdate=4 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=3 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200403181238/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12322301 |archive-date=3 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Sachdeva |first1=Sam |title=Clark's biking calamity a sign of wider confusion |url=https://www.newsroom.co.nz/2020/04/04/1114021/clarks-cycle-calamity-a-sign-of-wider-confusion |accessdate=4 April 2020 |work=[[Newsroom]] |date=4 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406102009/https://www.newsroom.co.nz/2020/04/04/1114021/clarks-cycle-calamity-a-sign-of-wider-confusion |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> Later, Clark admitted that he had driven his family twenty kilometres to a nearby beach in Dunedin for a walk during the first week in lockdown. Clark offered his resignation to Prime Minister Ardern, who turned it down due to his role in leading the Government's response to the COVID-19 pandemic. However, she stripped Clark of his ministerial portfolio as Associate Finance Minister and demoted him to the bottom of Labour's Cabinet list.<ref>{{cite news |title=David Clark offers to resign after revealing he took a trip to beach during Covid-19 lockdown |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/413617/david-clark-offers-to-resign-after-revealing-he-took-a-trip-to-beach-during-covid-19-lockdown |accessdate=7 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=7 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407052511/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/413617/david-clark-offers-to-resign-after-revealing-he-took-a-trip-to-beach-during-covid-19-lockdown |archive-date=7 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

In early April, a Christchurch man was arrested by police after posting a Facebook video of himself deliberately coughing and sneezing on customers at a [[FreshChoice]] supermarket. Ardern warned that people would be arrested for deliberately coughing on others.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Sadler |first1=Rachel |title=Coronavirus: Jacinda Ardern reveals people will be arrested for deliberately coughing on others |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/04/coronavirus-jacinda-ardern-reveals-people-will-be-arrested-for-deliberately-coughing-on-others.html |accessdate=5 April 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=5 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406075140/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/04/coronavirus-jacinda-ardern-reveals-people-will-be-arrested-for-deliberately-coughing-on-others.html |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Man films himself coughing on shoppers in supermarket |url=https://www.odt.co.nz/news/national/man-films-himself-coughing-shoppers-supermarket |accessdate=5 April 2020 |work=[[Otago Daily Times]] |date=4 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406075356/https://www.odt.co.nz/news/national/man-films-himself-coughing-shoppers-supermarket |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> The man pleaded guilty to a charge of offensive behaviour in the Christchurch District Court. He received a negative test for COVID-19. The man later apologised for his actions.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Lourens |first1=Marine |title=Supermarket cougher previously jailed for ill-considered prank |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/crime/120837754/man-in-court-after-coughing-on-christchurch-shoppers |accessdate=6 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=6 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406075445/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/crime/120837754/man-in-court-after-coughing-on-christchurch-shoppers |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Allott |first1=Amber |title=Christchurch man filmed coughing in supermarket apologises for 'foolish act' |url=https://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/news/christchurch/christchurch-man-filmed-coughing-in-supermarket-apologises-for-foolish-act/ |accessdate=6 April 2020 |work=[[Newstalk ZB]] |date=6 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406075534/https://www.newstalkzb.co.nz/news/christchurch/christchurch-man-filmed-coughing-in-supermarket-apologises-for-foolish-act/ |archive-date=6 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 7 April, it was reported that the [[New Zealand Police]] had recorded 291 breaches under the [[Civil Defence Emergency Management Act 2002]] and the [[Health Act 1956]]. Of these, 263 people had been issued with warnings for breaking lockdown rules, 12 had received a youth referral, and 16 were facing charges. Clark, who was disciplined by the prime minister for violating lockdown requirements, was not listed among the 291 breaches reported.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Te |first1=Mandy |title=People arrested, set to appear in court as lockdown rules ignored |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/crime/120871562/people-arrested-set-to-appear-in-court-as-lockdown-rules-ignored |accessdate=7 April 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=7 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407055923/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/crime/120871562/people-arrested-set-to-appear-in-court-as-lockdown-rules-ignored |archivedate=7 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Boyle |first1=Chelsea |last2=Hurley |first2=Sam |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Police record nearly 300 lockdown breaches, Health Minister David Clark not included |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12322928 |accessdate=7 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=7 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200407055803/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12322928 |archivedate=7 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 8 April, the [[Commissioner of Police (New Zealand)|Police Commissioner]] [[Andrew Coster]] updated the figures to 367 breaches including 45 prosecutions, 309 warnings, and 13 youth referrals. Coster also reported that Police were dealing with 37,000 breaches, mainly by businesses.<ref>{{cite news |title=NZers breaching lockdown 'more likely to be flouting the rules' – police |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413776/nzers-breaching-lockdown-more-likely-to-be-flouting-the-rules-police |accessdate=8 April 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=8 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200408080038/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/413776/nzers-breaching-lockdown-more-likely-to-be-flouting-the-rules-police |archivedate=8 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 21 April, a [[Queenstown, New Zealand|Queenstown]] man was sentenced to a concurrent sentence of one month imprisonment and two weeks' imprisonment for breaching lockdown restrictions and damaging a stainless steel toilet.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Roxburgh |first1=Tracey |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Month's jail for breaching rules despite four warnings |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326355 |accessdate=21 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=21 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200421003127/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326355 |archivedate=21 April 2020}}</ref> In Auckland, a 32-year-old woman who allegedly spat at [[Auckland Transport]] staff on a train was charged with assault under the [[Crimes Act 1961]]. Auckland Transport has reported of incidents of stopping people trying to travel from outlying suburbs like [[Henderson, New Zealand|Henderson]] and [[Takanini]] to shop in the city centre and groups of young people travelling on trains for non-essential reasons.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Woman charged over spitting at Auckland Transport staff on train |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326365 |accessdate=21 April 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=21 April 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200421003900/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12326365 |archivedate=21 April 2020}}</ref>

On 3 May, it was reported that Police had received 1,200 reports of people breaching Alert Level 3 restrictions. 686 of these reports were filed between 6 pm on 1 May and 6pm on 2 May. Police confirmed that they had taken enforcement action against 514 people for breaches of either the Health Act or the Civil Defence Emergency Act since Alert Level 3 came into force on midnight 28 April, prosecuting 135 and warning 342.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: 1200 public reports of people breaching the alert level 3 restrictions |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12329193 |accessdate=3 May 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=3 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200503003808/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12329193 |archivedate=3 May 2020}}</ref> Police Acting Assistant Commissioner Scott Fraser also announced that they had to close down hundreds of parties in the past few days since the Alert Level 3 lockdown came into force. He warned that illegal public gatherings would "waste all the sacrifices" others had to make to beat COVID-19.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Satherley |first1=Dan |title=Coronavirus: Hundreds of level 3 parties busted by police |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-hundreds-of-level-3-parties-busted-by-police.html |accessdate=3 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=3 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200503004511/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-hundreds-of-level-3-parties-busted-by-police.html |archivedate=3 May 2020}}</ref>

On 18 May, [[Commissioner of Police (New Zealand)|Police Commissioner]] [[Andrew Coster]] confirmed that the Police had received 250 reports of illegal mass gatherings in the four days since Alert Level 2 came into effect on 14 May. These included 30 reports of people holding or attending illegal parties; 29 of which resulted in a warning and one in a prosecution.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Burrows |first1=Matt |title=Coronavirus: 250 mass gatherings reported in New Zealand since alert level 2 shift |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-250-mass-gatherings-reported-in-new-zealand-since-alert-level-2-shift.html |accessdate=22 May 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=18 May 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200522051856/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/05/coronavirus-250-mass-gatherings-reported-in-new-zealand-since-alert-level-2-shift.html |archivedate=22 May 2020}}</ref>

====Managed isolation violations====
On 5 July, it was reported that a woman who had escaped managed isolation at the Pullman Hotel in Auckland had been apprehended and charged with breaching the 14-day isolation period under the [[COVID-19 Public Health Response Act 2020]]. The woman had arrived from Australia on 27 June.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Hutt |first1=Kendall |title=Coronavirus: Woman who escaped managed isolation in Auckland charged for breach |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300049527/coronavirus-woman-who-escaped-managed-isolation-in-auckland-charged-for-breach |accessdate=5 July 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=5 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200705090305/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300049527/coronavirus-woman-who-escaped-managed-isolation-in-auckland-charged-for-breach |archivedate=5 July 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Cheng |first1=Derek |title=Woman scaled two fences to escape managed isolation; Govt says no failure of process |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12345639 |accessdate=5 July 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=5 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200705090056/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12345639|archive-date=5 July 2020}}</ref>

On 8 July, a 32-year-old man, who had arrived from India, was charged with violating Section 26 (1) of the COVID-19 Public Health Response Act 2020 after he escaped managed isolation at the Stamford Plaza Hotel in central Auckland. He visited the [[Countdown (supermarket)|Countdown]] supermarket in Victoria Street before being located by security guards after 70 minutes. After the man tested positive for COVID-19, the supermarket closed temporarily with its staff entering into self-isolation.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Ward |first1=Lynley |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Retracing infected man's missing 70 minutes |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12346523 |accessdate=8 July 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=8 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200708063128/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12346523 |archivedate=8 July 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>

On 10 July, a man was arrested for violating the COVID-19 Public Health Response Act 2020 after he cut through a fence at a managed isolation facility at Distinction Hotel in [[Hamilton, New Zealand|Hamilton]] and visited a liquor store the previous night.<ref name="RNZ 10 July 2020">{{cite news |title=Man arrested after cutting through fence to escape Hamilton isolation facility On 11 July, a man in his 60s escaped a managed isolation facility at Waipuna Hotel in Auckland and knocked on the doors of three residents outside the facility. He was subsequently picked up by police and placed under armed guard at Waipuna Hotel.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Molyneux |first1=Vita |title=Person broke window, scaled fence in another escape from managed isolation |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/07/person-broke-window-fence-in-another-escape-from-managed-isolation.html |accessdate=11 July 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=11 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200711013229/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/07/person-broke-window-fence-in-another-escape-from-managed-isolation.html |archivedate=11 July 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Returnee 'in their late 60s' broke window, climbed fence to escape managed isolation – fourth to do so in a week |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/returnee-in-their-late-60s-broke-window-climbed-fence-escape-managed-isolation-fourth-do-so-week |accessdate=11 July 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=11 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200711065456/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/returnee-in-their-late-60s-broke-window-climbed-fence-escape-managed-isolation-fourth-do-so-week |archivedate=11 July 2020}}</ref>

On 25 July, it was reported that authorities had detained a family of five (comprising a mother and four children aged 12, 16, 17, and 18) for breaching managed isolation at the Distinction Hotel in Hamilton. The family had arrived from [[Brisbane]] in Australia on 21 July in order to attend a relative's funeral in Auckland. While the family's application for an exemption was being processed by the Health Ministry, they had escaped by breaking a window and scaling a fence. Four members of the family were apprehended by Police in a nearby park while the 17-year old had traveled to Auckland where he was detained by Police there. Government minister Woods has criticised the family breaking the rules, stating that "while we can understand their grief we can not let one tragedy to turn into a tragedy of hundreds." Four members of the family have been charged with breaching a Health Act notice.<ref>{{cite news |title=Megan Woods and Darryn Webb on Hamilton Covid isolation escapees mother and her 18-year-old daughter were sentenced to 14 days imprisonment by Judge Noel Sainsbury of the Auckland District Court.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Smith |first1=Anneke |title=Covid 19 about alleged "systematic racism" in the New Zealand justice system against [[Māori people|Māori]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Dillane |first1=Tom |title=Booze run vs father's funeral: questions of systemic racism over quarantine escapees' contrasting sentences |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12360481 |accessdate=4 September 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> [[New Zealand Public Party]] leader [[Billy Te Kahika]] has advocated on behalf of the woman and her family, also claiming credit for getting her sentence reduced by seven days.<ref name="National Rally 12 Sep 2020" />

On 30 July, a 32-year-old man, who had travelled from [[Brisbane]], was apprehended following a failed attempt to breach managed isolation at the Crowne Plaza in central Auckland. The man was charged under the COVID-19 Public Health Response Act.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 coronavirus: Brief escape from Auckland managed isolation hotel |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12352411 |accessdate=30 July 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=30 July 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200730052831/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12352411 |archivedate=30 July 2020}}</ref>

On 14 October, a 22-year-old woman was charged with allegedly trying to escape from Auckland's Grand Millennium Hotel during three incidents in October 2020.<ref>{{cite news |title=Woman charged allegedly escaping from the Grand Millennium Hotel |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/woman-charged-allegedly-escaping-from-the-grand-millennium-hotel/VEKO27AW3T6IJCVCO5F5Z2N44Q/ |accessdate=18 October 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=14 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201018111727/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/woman-charged-allegedly-escaping-from-the-grand-millennium-hotel/VEKO27AW3T6IJCVCO5F5Z2N44Q/ |archivedate=14 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

on 11 November, the [[West Indies cricket team]] were denied further training privileges after members breached managed isolation rules by mingling and sharing food while undergoing managed isolation at the "Chateau in the Park" hotel in Christchurch.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: West Indies cricket team flout quarantine rules; one new case |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-west-indies-cricket-team-flout-quarantine-rules-one-new-case/HCMV2GHUHQMHGCQXICAQV6LMFU/?ref=readmore |accessdate=12 November 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=11 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201112005458/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/covid-19-coronavirus-west-indies-cricket-team-flout-quarantine-rules-one-new-case/HCMV2GHUHQMHGCQXICAQV6LMFU/?ref=readmore |archivedate=12 November 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Leaks and misinformation====
In early July 2020, [[New Zealand National Party|National Party]] MP [[Hamish Walker]] admitted leaking the private details of COVID-19 patients to the media.<ref>{{cite news |last=Cooke|first=Henry|title= National MP Hamish Walker admits passing on leaked Covid-19 patient info from former party president Michelle Boag|url= https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/politics/300051710/national-mp-hamish-walker-admits-passing-on-leaked-covid19-patient-info-from-former-party-president-michelle-boag |accessdate=7 July 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=7 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200707100516/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/politics/300051710/national-mp-hamish-walker-admits-passing-on-leaked-covid19-patient-info-from-former-party-president-michelle-boag|archive-date=7 July 2020}}</ref> Former National Party President [[Michelle Boag]] had passed Walker the information in her capacity as chief executive of the [[Auckland Rescue Helicopter Trust]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=Small |first1=Zane |title=Former National Party president Michelle Boag admits passing COVID-19 patient details to MP Hamish Walker |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/07/former-national-party-president-michelle-boag-admits-passing-covid-19-patient-details-to-mp-hamish-walker.html |accessdate=7 July 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=7 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200707100614/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/politics/2020/07/former-national-party-president-michelle-boag-admits-passing-covid-19-patient-details-to-mp-hamish-walker.html|archive-date=7 July 2020}}</ref> Walker was stripped of his portfolios and later announced that he would not be contesting the 2020 general election.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid-19 privacy leak: MP Hamish Walker announces he won't stand for re-election |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/420754/covid-19-privacy-leak-mp-hamish-walker-announces-he-won-t-stand-for-re-election |accessdate=8 July 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=8 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200708003402/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/political/420754/covid-19-privacy-leak-mp-hamish-walker-announces-he-won-t-stand-for-re-election|archive-date=8 July 2020}}</ref> Boag, who also admitted leaking similar information to National MP [[Michael Woodhouse]], subsequently resigned from her position with the Helicopter Trust and her membership of the National Party.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/300053836/michelle-boag-leaves-national-party-after-leaking-patient-info-to-michael-woodhouse |title=Michelle Boag leaves National Party after leaking patient info to Michael Woodhouse |author=Thomas Coughlan |publisher=Stuff |date=10 July 2020 |accessdate=10 July 2020}}</ref>

On 18 August 2020, managed isolation and quarantine deputy chief executive Megan Main confirmed that a First Security guard had leaked information about the names, room numbers, and travel itineraries of returnees staying in managed isolation at Auckland's Sheraton Four Points managed isolation facility on [[Snapchat]]. Main apologised for the returnees' privacy breach. She also confirmed that the guard had been removed from duty at the hotel and that First Security was conducting an employment investigation into the guard.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Quinlivan |first1=Mark |title=Coronavirus: Managed isolation security guard leaks list of people staying at Auckland facility on Snapchat |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/08/coronavirus-managed-isolation-security-guard-leaks-list-of-people-staying-at-auckland-facility-on-snapchat.html |accessdate=18 August 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=18 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200818114711/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/08/coronavirus-managed-isolation-security-guard-leaks-list-of-people-staying-at-auckland-facility-on-snapchat.html |archivedate=18 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> That same day, the ''[[The New Zealand Herald]]'' reported that a man had admitted spreading a rumor on [[Reddit]] that a recent outbreak of commmunity transmissions in Auckland in mid-August had been caused by a family member supposedly entering a managed isolation facility. This rumor was dismissed by health authorities.<ref>{{cite news |title=Covid 19 Coronavirus: Man behind the vicious managed isolation breach rumour speaks |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12357396 |accessdate=30 August 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=18 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200828180145/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12357396 |archivedate=28 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Maritime travel breaches====
In late September, it was reported that three German yachties had defied New Zealand's COVID-19 laws by sailing from [[Tahiti]] to [[Opua]], [[Northland Region|Northland]] despite having their application for a border exemption denied by [[Immigration New Zealand]]. After being tested and quarantined on their vessel for 14 days, the three returned to Germany on 1 October and are subject to a travel ban from New Zealand. While Immigration New Zealand defended their decision, Rear Commodore Guy Chester of the Ocean Cruising Club expressed concerns about the plight of hundreds of yachties stranded in the Pacific, who were unable to dock in New Zealand and Australia due to COVID-19 border restrictions.<ref>{{cite news |title=German yachties had 'blatant disregard' for New Zealand law - Immigration NZ |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/427031/german-yachties-had-blatant-disregard-for-new-zealand-law-immigration-nz |accessdate=29 September 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=27 September 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200929081859/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/427031/german-yachties-had-blatant-disregard-for-new-zealand-law-immigration-nz|archive-date=29 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=German yachties jailed until flight on Thursday after being refused entry into NZ |url=https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/german-yachties-jailed-until-flight-thursday-after-being-refused-entry-into-nz |accessdate=29 September 2020 |work=[[1 News]] |date=29 September 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200929074405/https://www.tvnz.co.nz/one-news/new-zealand/german-yachties-jailed-until-flight-thursday-after-being-refused-entry-into-nz |archivedate=29 September 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Orsman |first1=Bernard |title=Covid 19 coronavirus: German crew who entered NZ unlawfully have flown home |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12369970 |accessdate=2 October 2020 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |date=2 October 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201002083638/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12369970 |archivedate=2 October 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

== Support bubble ==
[[File:Covid-19-Bubble-spread-02-1.gif|thumb|right|200px|The support bubble concept]]
Early on in the COVID-19 pandemic, New Zealand launched the support bubble concept.<ref>[https://thespinoff.co.nz/covid-19/01-04-2020/siouxsie-wiles-toby-morris-why-those-bubbles-are-so-important/ Siouxsie Wiles & Toby Morris: Why those bubbles are so important]</ref>
A bubble is defined as a group of people with whom you have close physical contact. People in a bubble do not have to practice social distancing from others within the same bubble. The entire bubble counts as one household.<ref>[https://www.bbc.com/news/health-52637354 ]</ref><ref>[https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2020/05/new-zealand-quarantine-bubble-concept-america.html ]</ref><ref>[https://theconversation.com/quarantine-bubbles-when-done-right-limit-coronavirus-risk-and-help-fight-loneliness-140134 ]</ref>

== Testing ==

=== Requirements ===
In early March 2020, there were concerns about COVID-19 tests being given only to people with symptoms who had returned from impacted countries or people who had been in contact with a confirmed case.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Morton|first=Jamie|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12313924|title=Coronavirus testing: Five questions answered|date=5 March 2020|work=[[The New Zealand Herald]]|access-date=14 March 2020|language=en-NZ|issn=1170-0777|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200305014210/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12313924|archive-date=5 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Some people with symptoms but who did not fit these categories were not tested.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120277695/coronavirus-auckland-mums-request-to-be-tested-for-virus-rejected|title=Coronavirus: Auckland mum's request to be tested for virus rejected|website=Stuff|language=en|access-date=14 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200314171609/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/120277695/coronavirus-auckland-mums-request-to-be-tested-for-virus-rejected|archive-date=14 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

The case definition for qualifying for a COVID-19 test is having "any acute respiratory infection with at least one of the following symptoms: cough, sore throat, shortness of breath, [[coryza]], [or] [[anosmia]] with or without fever."<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.health.govt.nz/system/files/documents/pages/covid-19_case_definition-3apr20.pdf|title=Case definition of COVID-19 infection – 3 April 2020|website=Ministry of Health NZ|date=3 April 2020|access-date=8 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200408020444/https://www.health.govt.nz/system/files/documents/pages/covid-19_case_definition-3apr20.pdf|archive-date=8 April 2020|url-status=dead}}</ref>

The previous case definition for testing from 14 March to 3 April was meeting at least one of the following criteria:<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.health.govt.nz/our-work/diseases-and-conditions/covid-19-novel-coronavirus/covid-19-novel-coronavirus-information-specific-audiences/covid-19-novel-coronavirus-resources-health-professionals/case-definition-covid-19-infection|title=Case definition of COVID-19 infection|website=Ministry of Health NZ|access-date=17 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200317031826/https://www.health.govt.nz/our-work/diseases-and-conditions/covid-19-novel-coronavirus/covid-19-novel-coronavirus-information-specific-audiences/covid-19-novel-coronavirus-resources-health-professionals/case-definition-covid-19-infection|archive-date=17 March 2020|url-status=unfit}}</ref>
* symptoms (fever ''or'' cough ''or'' shortness of breath ''or'' sore throat) ''and'' travel history
* symptoms (fever ''or'' cough ''or'' shortness of breath ''or'' sore throat) ''and'' close or causal contact with a suspect, probable or confirmed case
* healthcare workers with [[pneumonia]]
* people treated in [[intensive care unit]]s for severe respiratory illnesses

For cases not fitting this case definition doctors are encouraged to use their own judgement whether to test the patient or not.<ref>{{Cite news |url= https://www.newsroom.co.nz/2020/03/17/1086633?slug=pm-to-doctors-test-more-people-for-covid-19|title=PM to doctors: test more people for Covid-19|date=17 March 2020|website=[[Newsroom (website)|Newsroom]]|language=en-AU|access-date=17 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200729003849/https://www.newsroom.co.nz/2020/03/17/1086633?slug=pm-to-doctors-test-more-people-for-covid-19|archive-date=29 July 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 18 August, [[Newshub]] reported that a senior quarantine official had revealed that quarantine workers had requested a regular testing "regime" multiple times but their concerns were ignored. While Prime Minister Ardern had initially claimed that some workers were reluctant, Health Minister Chris Hipkins acknowledged that he was aware that the testing of border staff was incomplete during a briefing, stating that "they should not have been declined tests."  Opposition Leader Judith Collins criticised the Government's handling of the issue.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Morrah |first1=Michael |title=Coronavirus: Senior quarantine whistleblower says staff were refused regular testing programme despite pleas |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/08/coronavirus-senior-quarantine-whistleblower-says-staff-were-refused-regular-testing-programme-despite-pleas.html |accessdate=18 August 2020 |work=[[Newshub]] |date=18 August 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200818112407/https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/new-zealand/2020/08/coronavirus-senior-quarantine-whistleblower-says-staff-were-refused-regular-testing-programme-despite-pleas.html |archivedate=18 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Results ===

{{As of|2020|09|30}}, there have been 960,559 tests completed in total,<ref name="current cases"/> with a positivity rate of {{Percent|1480|960,559|2}}. {{As of|2020|09|27}}, the ethnic group with the highest rate of testing is Pacific, with 27.5% of that population being tested, followed by Māori with 15.9%, European/[[MELAA]]/Other with 13.9%, and finally Asian with 12.1%,{{Efn|The testing data is reported with prioritised ethnicity. If a person has multiple ethnicities, they are reported only as a single ethnicity with the following order of precedence: Māori, Pacific, Asian, Middle Eastern/Latin American/African, Other, European. This is in contrast to total response ethnicity, where a person with multiple ethnicities is reported under all ethnic groups they identify with.<ref>{{cite web |url= https://www.health.govt.nz/system/files/documents/publications/hiso-10001-2017-ethnicity-data-protocols-v2.pdf |title= HISO 10001:2017 Ethnicity Data Protocols |publisher=Ministry of Health |date= September 2017 |access-date= 23 May 2020 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20200218113435/https://www.health.govt.nz/system/files/documents/publications/hiso-10001-2017-ethnicity-data-protocols-v2.pdf |archive-date= 18 February 2020 |url-status= live }}</ref>|name=prio_ethnic|group=}} out of 746,478 people in total,<ref name="testing by region">{{cite web |title=COVID-19 – Testing by region |url=https://www.health.govt.nz/our-work/diseases-and-conditions/covid-19-novel-coronavirus/covid-19-current-situation/covid-19-current-cases/covid-19-testing-region |website=Health.govt.nz |publisher=New Zealand Government |accessdate=5 September 2020}}</ref> or {{percent|746,478|4,996,000|1}} of the New Zealand population of 4,996,000.<ref name="NZ population"/>

Starting from 16 April, random voluntary community testing took place in select supermarkets around the country to provide information on whether there still existed community transmission of the virus.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414454/random-testing-to-give-insight-into-covid-19-spread|title=Random testing to give insight into Covid-19 spread|first=Rowan|last=Quinn|work=Radio NZ|date=17 April 2020|accessdate=17 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200417025105/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/414454/random-testing-to-give-insight-into-covid-19-spread|archive-date=17 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121074955/coronavirus-wider-covid19-testing-starts-in-christchurch-community|title=Coronavirus: Wider Covid-19 testing starts in Christchurch, Waikato|first1=Michael|last1=Hayward|first2=Jo|last2=Lines-MacKenzie|date=17 April 2020|access-date=17 April 2020|work=Stuff|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200422060757/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/121074955/coronavirus-wider-covid19-testing-starts-in-christchurch-community|archive-date=22 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> This testing resulted in no positive results out of 1000 people by 20 April.<ref name="R0=0.48">{{cite news |author=Eleanor Ainge Roy |title=New Zealand plans to ease coronavirus lockdown in a week |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/20/new-zealand-plans-to-ease-coronavirus-lockdown-in-a-week |accessdate=21 April 2020 |work=The Guardian |date=20 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200420234845/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/apr/20/new-zealand-plans-to-ease-coronavirus-lockdown-in-a-week |archive-date=20 April 2020 |url-status=live }}</ref>{{update inline|When did it finish?|date=May 2020}}

No cases have been reported in the Chatham Islands,<ref name="Chathams Newsroom 6 April">{{cite web|title=Chatham Islands: hoping for early release from lockdown|url=https://www.newsroom.co.nz/2020/04/05/1114909/chatham-islands-hoping-for-early-release-from-lockdown |last=Kayes|first=Jim|date=6 April 2020|work=[[Newsroom (website)|Newsroom]]|accessdate=19 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200411203918/https://www.newsroom.co.nz/2020/04/05/1114909/chatham-islands-hoping-for-early-release-from-lockdown|archive-date=11 April 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Stewart Island,{{citation needed|date= April 2020}} New Zealand's [[Political status of the Cook Islands and Niue|associated states]] ([[Cook Islands]], [[Niue]]) or the dependent territory of [[Tokelau]].<ref name="WHO Dashboard">{{cite web|title=WHO COVID-19 Dashboard|url=https://covid19.who.int/|date=17 April 2020 |accessdate=17 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200416183953/https://covid19.who.int/|archive-date=16 April 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref>

During the lock down, overall weekly deaths declined in New Zealand compared to previous years.<ref name=":0">{{Cite web|title=Weekly deaths declined in NZ's lockdown – but we still don't know exactly why – Public Health Expert, University of Otago|url=https://blogs.otago.ac.nz/pubhealthexpert/2020/07/10/weekly-deaths-declined-in-nzs-lockdown-but-we-still-dont-know-exactly-why/|access-date=2020-08-09|language=en-NZ}}</ref> The decline is thought to be linked to a reduction in deaths from [[traffic collision]]s, [[air pollution]], [[Occupational safety and health|work injuries]], [[respiratory tract infection]]s, and [[elective surgery]].<ref name=":0" />

=== Clusters ===
[[File:Bluff - 27072304573.jpg|thumb|Oyster Cove, the venue of the Bluff wedding at [[Stirling Point]]]]
[[File:Rosewood Resthome 955 (cropped).jpg|thumb|Rosewood Rest Home in Christchurch, the cluster with the greatest number of deaths]]

{{as of|2020|11|17}}, the Ministry of Health had identified 18 significant [[Disease cluster|clusters]] of at least ten confirmed or probable COVID-19 cases.

There is currently one active significant cluster in New Zealand:<ref name="MOH Clusters">{{cite web |title=COVID-19 – Significant clusters |url=https://www.health.govt.nz/our-work/diseases-and-conditions/covid-19-novel-coronavirus/covid-19-current-situation/covid-19-current-cases/covid-19-significant-clusters |website=Ministry of Health NZ |date={{#time: j F Y}} |accessdate=22 August 2020}}</ref>

International Mariners, [[Christchurch]] – 33 ({{as of|2020|11|17}})

The following clusters have been closed. A cluster is considered closed when there have been no new cases for two incubation periods (i.e. 28 days) from the date when all cases complete isolation.<ref name="MOH Clusters"/>

*[[Auckland]] August cluster,<ref>{{cite news |last1=Martin |first1=Hannah |title=Coronavirus: Auckland cluster largest in NZ, PM warns of Covid's 'long tail' |url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300089545/coronavirus-auckland-cluster-largest-in-nz-pm-warns-of-covids-long-tail |accessdate=26 August 2020 |work=[[Stuff (website)|Stuff]] |date=24 August 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200826052024/https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/300089545/coronavirus-auckland-cluster-largest-in-nz-pm-warns-of-covids-long-tail|archive-date=26 August 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> closed 3 November 2020<ref>{{cite news |title=Five new Covid-19 cases in NZ today, Auckland August cluster closed |url=https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/429755/five-new-covid-19-cases-in-nz-today-auckland-august-cluster-closed |accessdate=12 November 2020 |work=[[Radio New Zealand]] |date=3 November 2020 |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20201109120822/https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/national/429755/five-new-covid-19-cases-in-nz-today-auckland-august-cluster-closed |archivedate=9 November 2020}}</ref> – 179
